APPENDIX A: CURRICULA VITAE (CV)	61

Executive summary 

Egis excels in providing independent verification and technical assurance services by combining global expertise with local knowledge to deliver thorough, impartial assessments. Our collaborative approach, backed by a track record of successfully verifying and assuring projects such as the Queensland Train Manufacturing Program and the High-Capacity Metro Trains, ensures adherence to the highest standards and instils client confidence in our integrity and quality.

The North East Link (NEL) project is a major infrastructure initiative in Melbourne, Australia. It involves constructing 6.5 km of tunnels to connect the Eastern Freeway to the M80 Ring Road. This project aims to reduce travel times by up to 35 minutes, take 15,000 trucks off local roads daily, and improve overall connectivity in Melbourne's north-east. It's part of Victoria's Big Build program and includes upgrades to existing roads, new cycling and walking paths, and enhanced public transport options.

This response outlines our approach to providing outstanding NEL IV Services to the State Tolling Corporation.

Conflict of Interest

Egis declares that a number of our  have had a long-standing social relationship with the STC Tolling Director, Zoltan Maklary 

Other than this association, as at the date of lodgement of its Tender, no actual or potential conflict of interest exists between Egis and any party engaged on the NEL project. 

Outline the processes which are in place to handle any future conflict of interest (actual or perceived).

Prior to undertaking any Services, all Egis IV Team personnel must undertake a probity induction. This induction will reinforce the compulsory Integrity eLearning training for the IV Team personnel as well as understanding, identifying and managing any conflicts of interest.

If any conflict of interest arises or is likely to arise, the EGIS Client Lead will immediately notify STC in writing of that conflict of interest or potential conflict of interest.

Fair Jobs Code

Compliance with Requirements 

Our understanding of Services

The State Tolling Corporation (STC) has proposed to develop an end-to-end solution for the Toll Collection Capability (TCC) that incorporates the delivery and operation of a Roadside System (RSS) and the delivery, support, and maintenance of a Back-Office system (BOS).

Program Services

Egis will submit an Independent Verifier (IV) Plan within 20 business days of commencement. This plan will be agreed with STC and will detail:

Skills, expertise and experience of the resources and the estimated resource levels required for each component of the Services,

Progress reports to be provided to the Project Control Group (PCG), and

A verification audit program to monitor performance of the Contractors’ obligations under the TCC.

Requirements Phase Services

Egis will provide STC with an independent, expert opinion on whether the specified technical and business requirements— including the Scope of Works and Technical Requirements (SWTRs)— have been accurately translated into robust, verifiable requirements.  

We will ensure that TCC Contractors implement strong processes to capture specialist engineering requirements, such as safety, human factors, Reliability, Availability and Maintainability (RAM), and cyber security. These requirements will complement the SWTRs and are typically gathered through workshops with subject matter experts from the operational community.  

All technical requirements must be captured in a centralised repository that serves as the single source of truth. If the project uses a Requirements Management Database (RMDB) such as IBM DOORS, we can provide specialist resources to set up the RMDB and develop templates and tools for tracking and managing requirements. Additionally, we can offer training for both STC and TCC Contractor staff on how to use these tools effectively.  

We will review the Requirements Verification Traceability Matrices (RVTMs) to ensure that verification evidence is captured at each stage of the project lifecycle. This will provide early assurance that all requirements have been adequately verified and highlight any gaps or 'orphans' that need to be addressed.

Design Phase Services

We will conduct document reviews for each of the TCC Contract design deliverables in accordance with the Project Delivery Schedule and will provide structured feedback for items that do not meet the specified requirements. 

Egis will also advise STC when each deliverable is suitable for endorsement or acceptance under the terms of the TCC Contracts.

Test Phase Services

We will provide specialist staff to witness specified tests and demonstrations, ensuring that the requirements needing verification through these methods are satisfactorily met.  

Additionally, we will provide ongoing updates on the maturity of the RVTMs and offer advice on when the Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to confirm that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been fulfilled.

Implementation and Operational Readiness Phase Services

Operational readiness is typically the responsibility of the Project Integrator, working with the Operator. Egis will tap into our experience in previous projects to support the operational readiness planning and ensure that the transition from Project to Operations happens seamlessly.

Our approach to test witnessing 

Egis conducts all test witnessing activities with a clearly defined set of objectives, which include; 

the verification of test results, 

assurance of compliance, 

ensuring documentation traceability, and 

identification & mitigation of risks. 

We conduct thorough technical reviews of test plans, schedules, and performance or functional requirements. These reviews help identify critical test cases, potential compliance issues, and operational deficiencies, enabling us to provide constructive feedback. We will develop a test witness schedule focused on these critical test cases to ensure that suitably experienced technical witnesses are present as needed.

Test witnessing observations are systematically collected and categorised according to the established objectives, then communicated concisely to the project. Responses, resulting controls, and any changes to test plans will be tracked to ensure risk mitigation and closure of observations.

Egis coordinates closely with the project team to ensure comments and observations are directed to the relevant forums and escalation levels. Our approach is adaptable, and we will tailor the process to best support the project by adding or removing scope based on stakeholder requirements, or adjusting outputs to align with existing project systems

Approach to GORC and its application 

Egis will implement a structured and proactive approach to General Overview and Reasonable Checking (GORC) throughout all stages of the project, ensuring full compliance with the technical, assurance, and contractual requirements set out in the TCC Contracts. The IV team will be led by a dedicated management team, with experience applying GORC practices on major Victorian transport projects such as the High Capacity Metro Trains (HCMT) and X’Trapolis 2 (XT2) Technical advisor roles, ensuring that personnel have the requisite expertise and accreditation to fulfil obligations. Egis’ approach is to provide continuous oversight, identify potential issues early, and resolve them promptly, minimising risks and ensuring the successful deployment of the tolling system. 

The IV Plan, along with supporting procedures, will be developed and submitted within 20 days of commencement to outline methodologies for meeting key performance and traceability requirements. Project risks will be organised by discipline, with risk ratings providing guidance for resourcing efforts. This approach will help prioritize key aspects of the project and determine the necessary actions as outlined for the QTMP IC project in Section 8, "Risk Management," of this proposal. These ratings will be reviewed and adjusted as the project evolves by the IC management team in consultation with STC representatives. A Completion Plan will be developed in line with the contractor’s documents which outlines the information required for the IV to make progressive assessments of each Critical Interface Milestone. 

Regular progress reports, governance meetings and audits will inform decision-making and enable prompt resolution of issues. Close communication with the STC and all stakeholders along with updates to the Services Delivery Management Plan on a 6 monthly basis will ensure alignment and facilitate early intervention when necessary.

Management Plans, Requirements, and Design Documents

During the requirements and design review stage of the project, Egis will review the TCC Contractors’ management plans, including technical specifications, quality assurance strategies, risk management plans and schedules. This will ensure that these plans align with the TCC Contracts and provide a realistic foundation for successful project delivery. 

We will assess the consistency of these documents with broader NEL tollway objectives, ensuring that they comply with legal, regulatory, and contractual requirements. Specialist design reviewers will evaluate compliance with the project requirements and relevant reference documents and tap into Egis’ international expertise as required.

Testing 

As the project progresses to the testing phase, Egis will ensure that test plans comprehensively cover all technical and functional requirements outlined in the TCC Contracts. Our testing and commissioning experts will witness tests and evaluate results to confirm the system performs as expected and meets relevant standards, ensuring the tolling system meets performance criteria before operational deployment.  

IV Testing Reviewers will assess the implementation of these plans, review the Contractors' records for completeness, and ensure the Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to verify that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been met.

Operational Readiness 

During the operational readiness phase, Egis will ensure that systems, processes, and personnel are fully prepared for tolling operations by assessing the compliance of the TCC Contractors to their management plans and the project’s contractual and operational requirements and ensuring that activities such as user training, support systems and maintenance protocols are in place.  

Capacity and Capability

Please outline your organisation’s knowledge and experience of delivering independent verifier services in the context of Victorian Government procurement processes applied to major projects (particularly transportation infrastructure projects):

Egis has a long track record of successfully delivering transportation infrastructure projects across Australia, including strategic planning, technical assurance and IV. We have extensive knowledge and experience working with Victorian Government clients and have successfully delivered projects for DTP, RSD and MTM, but we have not delivered IV services in Victoria. 

The following projects demonstrate our considerable experience in delivering IV and technical assurance services for various Australian state government agencies: 

Regional Rail Project Independent Certifier, Australia (2019 - current)

Egis has partnered with APP Corporation to provide IC services for the NSW Regional Rail Project fleet being delivered by Momentum Trains under a $2.8B public partnership for Transport for NSW. As the IC, we review and verify the design documentation, manufacture, testing and commissioning of the new rolling stock fleet. Our review of verification activities through the design, manufacturing and testing phases culminates in Certification of Acceptance of the rolling stock before the new fleet is placed into service. 

Brisbane Metro Independent Project Verifier (2016 – current)

Egis is the independent project verifier for the Brisbane Metro Vehicle and the Charging Infrastructure of the Brisbane Metro Project. We reviewed and verified the planning documentation, design, manufacture, testing and commissioning the Metro Vehicle and the Charging Infrastructure and ensured that the project is being delivered in accordance with the Design and Build Deed, the Performance Specification and the relevant Australian Design Rules, Disability Access and Performance Based Standards.

Queensland Train Manufacturing Program (QTMP) Independent Certification (2023 – current)

Egis and SYSTRA Australia Pty. Ltd. formed a Joint Venture to deliver the IC Services for the $9.5B Queensland Government funded QTMP. The project shall deliver 65 new passenger trains to operate on the South-East Queensland rail network, and includes the maintenance and stabling facility at Ormeau and a train manufacturing facility at Torbanlea. The role includes review of all design and test documentation, as well as to conduct surveillance and monitoring activities to certify that the Contractor’s Project Documentation and Project activities (e.g. tests) comply with the defined set of contractual requirements.

Queensland New Generation Rollingstock Accessibility Variation Project Independent Certification (2019 – 2024)

Egis provided independent certification for the design and testing of a suite of 14 modifications packages for the New Generation Rollingstock Operational Readiness Program. With a primary focus on the design stage of the project, the project called on our subject matter experts for the verification of interior-toilets, carbody shell, interior-saloon interior and gangways, brakes and heating, ventilation and air-conditioning.

High Capacity Metro Trains (HCMT) Project Technical Assurance, Victoria (2017 – current)

Egis is the technical advisor for the HCMT Project, the $2.3B public-private partnership (PPP) between the Victorian Government and Evolution Rail. Our role covers all aspects of the design and manufacture of the rolling stock, including providing subject matter experts for all train sub-systems and simulators. Our specialist technical capabilities allowed the application of full systems assurance and associated reliability, availability, maintainability and safety activities throughout the delivery phase of the project, as well as testing and commissioning of both the specialist equipment and the systems as a whole.

Please outline your organisation’s knowledge and experience of delivering independent verifier services in the context of complex technology-based business system projects:

Egis has extensive experience in delivering complex, technology-based services both globally and in Australia. By tapping into our global network for specialized expertise and support, we enhance project outcomes as demonstrated with major initiatives like the (Name major project). Relevant projects include:

Roatex Indonesia Toll System (Indonesia); 2024 - current

Egis Indonesia was appointed in early 2024 as an Independent Supervisory Consultant (ISC) for a PPP Project between the Hungarian government, through Roatex, and the Government of Indonesia. The Project will implement the first Multi-Lane Free Flow (MLFF) technology across all toll road sections in Indonesia. As the ISC, Egis will provide monitoring, supervision, reporting, and quality assurance Services to ensure that the Project is delivered in accordance with the defined standards. 

Clark Airport Expansion (Philippines) 

The Clark Airport Expansion Project, started in 2018, included the design, development and construction of a new Passenger Terminal Building (100,000sqm), designed for throughput of 8 million passengers per year. Egis, with its partner DCCD Engineering, was appointed as the Independent Consultant for the engineering, procurement and construction at Clark Airport for the three-year contract. Egis supported the Client with independent review through the project phases, from design review, through construction and procurement of systems and equipment, testing and commissioning of the new terminal and Operational Readiness and Airport Transition of the New Passenger Terminal Building and its landside support facilities.

Manila LRT Line 1 Extension (Philippines)  

Starting in 2015, the LRT Line 1 was extended from Baclaran Station to Niog Station in Bacoor, Cavite, a distance of 11.7 km. Of this length, 10.5 km was to be elevated and 1.2 km at-grade. The integrated LRT 1 has a total length of approximately 32.4 km and is operated and maintained by the Light Rail Manila Corporation.   Egis Rail, as the leader of the ERIGPHI joint venture, provided Independent Consultancy Services to the client, the Department of Transportation (Philippines).

Stony Point Communications Upgrade Project

Egis Omada was selected by MTM as the primary contractor to undertake the signalling design for the Stony Point Communications Upgrade project. The Stony Point line is one of the first rail lines ever to open in Melbourne and is part of the greater-metropolitan commuter rail network. 

North East Link Project (AUSTRALIA); 2021 - Current

Egis Omada has successfully delivered signalling design for the North East Link Project. As part of the rail interface works, the signalling arrangement and systems required modification and upgrades to ensure signalling assets were relocated outside of the proposed tunnel area.  Egis Omada’s scope of work included modification of the existing signalling arrangement, replacement of life-expired geographical interlocking with a new computer-based interlocking and upgrade of existing signal assets.  All signalling design was completed on time, on schedule and on budget to ensure construction work could be undertaken.  

Key Delivery Individual 

As an experienced Program Director, Systems Engineer, Test Engineer and Business Development professional, Richard has extensive analysis, specialist engineering, flight test, software integration and delivery management experience in the defence, telecommunications, financial and transport sectors. He thrives on building and leading teams and processes to consistently deliver solutions on-time and budget in complex and challenging environments. His direct and focussed style is aimed at removing blockers and holding all stakeholders critical to success accountable for their contributions to deliver the desired business outcomes. This is coupled with a strong sense of ownership and accountability, leading by example to create a high-performance culture.

As the Client Lead, Richard will focus on leading the Egis team to deliver IV Services to support STC’s primary objective of delivering an end-to-end solution for the TCC. Richard will focus on working with the stakeholders to set up the processes for:

A culture of trust and respect – building a foundation of trust forms the basis of working towards best-for-project outcomes.

Effective conflict resolution – large, complex technical projects will invariably include several strong personalities with strong opinions. Richard will ensure that his team approaches disagreements constructively and ’plays the ball, not the person’ to ensure an enduring positive working relationship. 

Role clarity – Richard will work with the parties to ensure that roles and responsibilities are clear early, to avoid any confusion or items ’falling through the cracks’ during the life of the project.

Effective escalation and resolution – Every project will experience issues. It is how they are resolved that will determine success. Richard will support the development of effective governance, and risk and issues resolution processes to enable speedy resolution, thereby promoting schedule adherence.

Richard’s engagement will then phase down to that required for effective oversight of the team, regular reporting and communication with the STC and Project stakeholders and the resolution of any issues.

Risk Management

Please provide sufficient evidence and experience from similar projects to demonstrate an understanding of the risks, issues and opportunities that commonly arise and how the identified risks were managed:

Egis Oceania has extensive experience managing commercial and project risk for our public and private sector clients. Egis Oceania's capabilities include the identification and quantification of infrastructure project related risks including design, construction and commissioning risk; operational risk; market risk; network and interface risk; industrial relations risk; and asset ownership risk (including residual risk). We are also familiar with the mechanisms of risk transfer and the role of risk allocation and value-for-money in tender evaluations. The generic structure of our risk management processes are aligned with AS/NZS 31000 2009: Risk Management.  At appropriate stages in complex projects, we facilitate risk management workshops (using an established methodology, an agreed risk register template and an agreed scale of likelihoods, impacts and consequences). Risk Management workshops will focus on areas of risk relevant to the particular project including: commercial risk, service delivery risk, reputational risk, project timing, technical quality and stakeholder relationships. For each new engagement, following the project inception meeting Egis will facilitate a risk management workshop with the relevant Project Stakeholders to establish the initial risk register and rate the risks using the scale of likelihoods, impacts and consequences, and with risk owners identified and with defined risk mitigation strategies.  

Identified risks will be assessed as to their priority to be managed. 

Egis have successfully delivered similar services, such as QTMP IC, we did this with our tried-and-true Risk Based Approach (RBA). As we are on QTMP, Egis will undertake a high-level assessment to rank identified risks associated with each Project and Design requirement in terms of consequence and likelihood. This will determine the level and type of review needed for each requirement and support a robust and repeatable evidence-based assessment across all requirements. Requirements defined as medium and high risk (see figure x) will be subject to a more intensive level of compliance assessment. This rating process is critical to form the basis for the design reviews, certification of design packages and identification/resolution of Potential, Actual and Minor Non-Compliances. 

If the Key Stakeholders disagree with the level of risk associated with a design requirement and the level of compliance assessment effort to be applied, our IV team will work collaboratively with those organisations to align/agree the risk allocation. If the level of risk associated with any requirement is unclear, a more conservative view will be taken i.e. a higher risk ranking will be assigned, and our team will apply the commensurate level of effort in our review and assessment. 

Egis will assess and rate the risks associated with each design package to determine the level of rigour we will apply in the certification process for each package and in monitoring controls that are applied. This supports an agile and efficient approach to compliance assessment, targeting allocation of our resources to ensure the level of effort and type of assessment is proportionate to the risk associated with a particular design package or deliverable, in achieving the objectives of the Project. 

Quality Management Systems

Our ISO:9001-certified Quality Management Systems (QMS) are built on a foundation of clear scope, project execution plans, regular project meetings, task breakdowns, and budgets for each project team. We ensure quality through peer reviews of all deliverables, monthly internal reviews with the Egis Project Director, and external reporting to our clients.  

Project managers are responsible for embedding Quality Assurance (QA) into the project workflow, including resource allocation, scheduling QA activities, and conducting design reviews at critical stages to verify calculations, assumptions, and compliance with specifications. As projects are dynamic and changes are inevitable, effective change management is a key factor in our success. We ensure that changes and risks are communicated regularly and promptly, enhancing stakeholder engagement and facilitating proactive issue resolution. This approach allows us to update project plans and baselines, ensuring potential impacts are addressed swiftly and supporting on-time delivery and project success.  

We understand that the quality management process must align with the customer or stakeholder’s needs. This helps define the required quality management processes and performance measurements. Our focus is on maintaining quality consistency throughout the project while remaining flexible and agile to meet shifting demands. Ultimately, our project quality management approach ensures that the project meets its intended objectives and delivers customer satisfaction. 

Examples of the ways in which Egis will work to achieve the best possible fitness for purpose on our clients’ projects include: 

Taking time to understand the underlying project drivers and critical issues that will make the project a success for our clients. 

Proactively scheduling and making time for opportunities for our clients to provide feedback on our work and for contractors, partners, and other consultants to provide their own comments and input. 

Issuing draft documents and work in progress (WIP) drawings/models and actively seeking and taking onboard feedback so we can contribute towards achieving overall project objectives. 

Taking a collaborative approach to reviews ensures that the process enhances the overall outcomes. 

Working collaboratively with our clients’ teams and project delivery partners using digital platforms and environments.  Our project quality management consists of three major processes:                                                                      

Quality Management Planning: Our quality planning focuses on taking all the information available at the beginning of the project and resolving how we will measure quality, establish KPIs, and prevent rework. This involves identifying the quality requirements and standards required for our projects. The project quality management process is clearly shared with all stakeholders, and appropriate tasks are delegated to those responsible to ensure the required outcomes.                                                                                                             

Quality Control: This involves ascertaining the review, approval requirements for the validation and verification of all deliverables prior to issuing to the client.                                                                                

Quality Assurance: This involves monitoring, auditing, and recording the results of quality activities to assess performance and recommend and implement necessary changes. Egis views effective quality management as a tool to increase competitiveness and performance and ensure constant change and improvement.

Are the quality systems certified?    No

If the answer to the above is ‘Yes’, what Australian or International standards apply:

Egis Oceania operates under an integrated HSEQ management system that consists of the following comprehensive third-party accredited system elements: Quality Management System, complying with ISO 9001 Environmental Management System, complying with ISO 14001 Occupational Health & Safety Management System, complying with AS/NZS 4801.

Process methodologies

Please outline your organisation’s experience of delivering independent verifier services under Victorian Government procurement processes with respect to ensuring a product, system or service complies with Requirements and Deliverables:

Internal systems and processes Egis utilises to deliver our projects to time, scope and budget include:

Nominated project management team: The project management team organises and prepares the contract execution plan, including rights and obligations, key milestones, services and deliverables, input data to be collected, applicable regulations and standards, communications plan, risks and opportunities, health and safety, corporate social responsibility, and ethics. They also ensure project objectives are met, track performance, and build team morale. Project Directors, Project Managers, and Commercial Managers are responsible for leading teams, managing resources, and ensuring that learning is transferred across projects.

Financial management: The project manager utilises a bottom-up budgeting tool called Project Toolbox, which is used for project scoping and pricing. This tool provides a detailed breakdown of all costs to be incurred on the project, enabling the tracking of tasks and budgets. 

Work package brief: This is a document recording the scope and inputs/outputs for specific project tasks with budget allocation and expected timeframes and quality assurance requirements.

Discipline-specific program: Programs are completed for each stage of the work and aligned with the master program.

Project issues register: This repository is used for recording the project issues, updated weekly, and then used to inform progress reports. 

Contract progress reports: We provide regular progress reporting to our clients and team to report on work completed, proposed work for the next period, any new risks and issues and further information required.

Project meetings: Internal project meetings are used to discuss progress, work accomplished, planned work, technical issues, and potential scope changes, as well as to identify any risks or problems that could impact project delivery. Project Managers and relevant line managers discuss conflicts regarding resourcing and project priorities. 

Internal reviews: We perform staged and timely internal project reviews to minimise the risk of re-work and ensure that an appropriate level of technical expertise is assigned at the project's outset.  

Please outline your organisation’s familiarity with and direct experience of providing independent verifier services for projects managed in accordance with the Project Development and Construction Management Act 1994 (Vic)(public construction):

Past performance and current work

Proven methodology

Egis has a proven track record and significant experience (XX+ years) delivering IV services on major transport projects in Australia and internationally.

Egis has a developed methodology for successfully delivering IV services. Our approach is based on a proven methodology that has consistently delivered results across multiple high-profile projects. This methodology incorporates best practices, robust tools, and lessons learned from comparable initiatives.

Egis has a solid foundation in managing IV specific document management systems, automated review and certification workflows, as well as advanced reporting and surveillance tools. These capabilities ensure greater efficiency and cost-effective delivery of IV services for NEL.

Our deep experience in both project delivery and IV equips us with a comprehensive understanding of the required services, the design approval process, and the complexities involved in addressing multiple stakeholder requirements on complex tolling projects. 

The below are the four key features which define the Egis certification approach:

Structured and Robust approach.  We will articulate a clear, specific, and logical process for certification that is repeatable across all design packages, construction milestones and completion procedures. Over the course of a long program of work, this consistency will allow all parties to understand what is expected and tailor their work methods to suit. 

Risk-based and appropriately resourced. We will ensure appropriate resourcing for the specific tasks at hand.  Each assessment will be made objectively with effort required to be proportionate to the risk associated if the task is not completed.

Collaborative yet independent. We will work transparently with all stakeholders (through continual and proactive dialogue; objectivity, and informal assistance with early issues identification and resolution). In doing so, it, will ensure it remains independent, consistent, and non-biased throughout the certification process. Effective collaboration between project stakeholders will be critical to the success of the overall project. Egis will implement a collaborative culture and facilitate opportunities to discuss solutions across various packages. This will be achieved through:

Active and collaborative problem solving.

Formal and informal dialogue.

A culture of sharing knowledge and information e.g. results of any on-site or off-site inspection, defect reporting, testing and audits regarding quality or compliance including any actual or potential non-compliance; An attitude of connected team, rather than ‘us’ and ‘them’ to foster an effective and efficient working behaviour Ensuring ownership of the project delivery remains with the delivery contractors while the IV team has the mechanism with which it can provide independent scrutiny across the design delivery process. The cohesive working environment will enhance confidence by delivery contractors in the IV process and vice versa.

Evidence-based certification methodology.  We will ensure that an evidence-based approach is used to test our work, prior to an IV review and certification occurring.

Reporting

A core requirement of efficiently delivering these aspects of the IV services is an accurate single source of truth, with Quality processes embedded into the workflows managed by online tools and systems. As well as managing workflows and the significant volume of documents associated with the IV services. This will inform key deliverables like the Progress Report to the Project stakeholders. 

For example, our central comments register created by Power BI can be analysed in terms of progress against key metrics, with the performance data visualised in a dashboard for tracking and reporting. 

Improvement

Over the life of the IV services and NEL, Egis is committed to continuous improvement and seeking opportunities for innovation. As new technology or systems become available that provide benefits and efficiencies in delivery of IV services, Egis will consider opportunities for automation of key tasks (e.g. reviewing design packages, managing/closing out comments) and potential use of artificial intelligence. If new digital tools and systems are fit for our purpose and offer efficiency benefits to the IV team, we will introduce them with the appropriate level of assurance, as part of a shared learning journey.

Social Procurement

Indirect Expenditure via Social Benefit Suppliers

Egis is committed to supporting Indigenous entrepreneurship and business development. We actively prioritise engaging with Indigenous and Torres Strait Islander businesses, particularly in indirect expenditure categories such as office supplies, catering, cleaning, training, and printing. This approach not only contributes to the economic success of Indigenous communities but also creates long-term social benefits.

We:

Prioritise purchasing from Indigenous enterprises where possible, including sourcing PPE from SupplyAus Holdings, stationary from Gulbari, and publishing/printing services from Iscariot Media.

Partner with organisations like Deadly Coders and offer Cultural Awareness Training delivered by First Nations trainers.

Work with Supply Nation to procure office supplies and IT equipment from verified Indigenous-owned businesses.

These initiatives align with our broader commitment to our Reconciliation Action Plan (RAP), fostering relationships with First Nations communities and businesses. By continuing to engage with Indigenous suppliers, we support their growth and provide meaningful opportunities for economic participation. Should we be successful in the North East Link project, we will further expand our engagement with local First Nations suppliers, further strengthening the Indigenous business community in Victoria.

Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) Strategy and Gender Inclusive Policy

Egis is committed to fostering a diverse and inclusive workplace. Our DEI strategy, focused on First Nations, Disability, Gender, Rainbow, and Culture, aims to create an environment where all employees can thrive.

Our gender inclusivity initiatives include:

Aiming to increase female representation across the workforce from 31.3% to 33% and leadership from 25.2% to 27% by 2025.

Addressing the gender pay gap and promoting career development for women.

Supporting families through a strong parental leave policy that provides flexibility.

We actively implement DEI initiatives through our employee-led DEI Network, which drives events such as International Women’s Day and NAIDOC Week. Egis is also compliant with the Australian Workplace Gender Equality Act, and we regularly monitor our progress towards closing gender gaps and promoting diversity at all levels. Our efforts ensure an inclusive workplace that values equality, creating opportunities for all employees to succeed and contribute to a high-performance culture.

Executive summary 

Egis excels in providing independent verification and technical assurance services by combining global expertise with local knowledge to deliver thorough, impartial assessments. Our collaborative approach, backed by a track record of successfully verifying and assuring projects such as the Queensland Train Manufacturing Program and the High-Capacity Metro Trains, ensures adherence to the highest standards and instils client confidence in our integrity and quality.

The North East Link (NEL) project is a major infrastructure initiative in Melbourne, Australia. It involves constructing 6.5 km of tunnels to connect the Eastern Freeway to the M80 Ring Road. This project aims to reduce travel times by up to 35 minutes, take 15,000 trucks off local roads daily, and improve overall connectivity in Melbourne's north-east. It's part of Victoria's Big Build program and includes upgrades to existing roads, new cycling and walking paths, and enhanced public transport options.

This response outlines our approach to providing outstanding NEL IV Services to the State Tolling Corporation.

Outline the processes which are in place to handle any future conflict of interest (actual or perceived).

Prior to undertaking any Services, all Egis IV Team personnel must undertake a probity induction. This induction will reinforce the compulsory Integrity eLearning training for the IV Team personnel as well as understanding, identifying and managing any conflicts of interest.

If any conflict of interest arises or is likely to arise, the EGIS Client Lead will immediately notify STC in writing of that conflict of interest or potential conflict of interest.

Fair Jobs Code

Compliance with Requirements 

Our understanding of Services

The State Tolling Corporation (STC) has proposed to develop an end-to-end solution for the Toll Collection Capability (TCC) that incorporates the delivery and operation of a Roadside System (RSS) and the delivery, support, and maintenance of a Back-Office system (BOS).

Program Services

Egis will submit an Independent Verifier (IV) Plan within 20 business days of commencement. This plan will be agreed with STC and will detail:

Skills, expertise and experience of the resources and the estimated resource levels required for each component of the Services,

Progress reports to be provided to the Project Control Group (PCG), and

A verification audit program to monitor performance of the Contractors’ obligations under the TCC.

Requirements Phase Services

Egis will provide STC with an independent, expert opinion on whether the specified technical and business requirements— including the Scope of Works and Technical Requirements (SWTRs)— have been accurately translated into robust, verifiable requirements.  

We will ensure that TCC Contractors implement strong processes to capture specialist engineering requirements, such as safety, human factors, Reliability, Availability and Maintainability (RAM), and cyber security. These requirements will complement the SWTRs and are typically gathered through workshops with subject matter experts from the operational community.  

All technical requirements must be captured in a centralised repository that serves as the single source of truth. If the project uses a Requirements Management Database (RMDB) such as IBM DOORS, we can provide specialist resources to set up the RMDB and develop templates and tools for tracking and managing requirements. Additionally, we can offer training for both STC and TCC Contractor staff on how to use these tools effectively.  

We will review the Requirements Verification Traceability Matrices (RVTMs) to ensure that verification evidence is captured at each stage of the project lifecycle. This will provide early assurance that all requirements have been adequately verified and highlight any gaps or 'orphans' that need to be addressed.

Design Phase Services

We will conduct document reviews for each of the TCC Contract design deliverables in accordance with the Project Delivery Schedule and will provide structured feedback for items that do not meet the specified requirements. 

Egis will also advise STC when each deliverable is suitable for endorsement or acceptance under the terms of the TCC Contracts.

Test Phase Services

We will provide specialist staff to witness specified tests and demonstrations, ensuring that the requirements needing verification through these methods are satisfactorily met.  

Additionally, we will provide ongoing updates on the maturity of the RVTMs and offer advice on when the Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to confirm that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been fulfilled.

Implementation and Operational Readiness Phase Services

Operational readiness is typically the responsibility of the Project Integrator, working with the Operator. Egis will tap into our experience in previous projects to support the operational readiness planning and ensure that the transition from Project to Operations happens seamlessly.

Our approach to test witnessing 

Egis conducts all test witnessing activities with a clearly defined set of objectives, which include; 

the verification of test results, 

assurance of compliance, 

ensuring documentation traceability, and 

identification & mitigation of risks. 

We conduct thorough technical reviews of test plans, schedules, and performance or functional requirements. These reviews help identify critical test cases, potential compliance issues, and operational deficiencies, enabling us to provide constructive feedback. We will develop a test witness schedule focused on these critical test cases to ensure that suitably experienced technical witnesses are present as needed.

Test witnessing observations are systematically collected and categorised according to the established objectives, then communicated concisely to the project. Responses, resulting controls, and any changes to test plans will be tracked to ensure risk mitigation and closure of observations.

Egis coordinates closely with the project team to ensure comments and observations are directed to the relevant forums and escalation levels. Our approach is adaptable, and we will tailor the process to best support the project by adding or removing scope based on stakeholder requirements, or adjusting outputs to align with existing project systems

Approach to GORC and its application 

Egis will implement a structured and proactive approach to General Overview and Reasonable Checking (GORC) throughout all stages of the project, ensuring full compliance with the technical, assurance, and contractual requirements set out in the TCC Contracts. The IV team will be led by a dedicated management team, with experience applying GORC practices on major Victorian transport projects such as the High Capacity Metro Trains (HCMT) and X’Trapolis 2 (XT2) Technical advisor roles, ensuring that personnel have the requisite expertise and accreditation to fulfil obligations. Egis’ approach is to provide continuous oversight, identify potential issues early, and resolve them promptly, minimising risks and ensuring the successful deployment of the tolling system. 

The IV Plan, along with supporting procedures, will be developed and submitted within 20 days of commencement to outline methodologies for meeting key performance and traceability requirements. Project risks will be organised by discipline, with risk ratings providing guidance for resourcing efforts. This approach will help prioritize key aspects of the project and determine the necessary actions as outlined for the QTMP IC project in Section 8, "Risk Management," of this proposal. These ratings will be reviewed and adjusted as the project evolves by the IC management team in consultation with STC representatives. A Completion Plan will be developed in line with the contractor’s documents which outlines the information required for the IV to make progressive assessments of each Critical Interface Milestone. 

Regular progress reports, governance meetings and audits will inform decision-making and enable prompt resolution of issues. Close communication with the STC and all stakeholders along with updates to the Services Delivery Management Plan on a 6 monthly basis will ensure alignment and facilitate early intervention when necessary.

Management Plans, Requirements, and Design Documents

During the requirements and design review stage of the project, Egis will review the TCC Contractors’ management plans, including technical specifications, quality assurance strategies, risk management plans and schedules. This will ensure that these plans align with the TCC Contracts and provide a realistic foundation for successful project delivery. 

We will assess the consistency of these documents with broader NEL tollway objectives, ensuring that they comply with legal, regulatory, and contractual requirements. Specialist design reviewers will evaluate compliance with the project requirements and relevant reference documents and tap into Egis’ international expertise as required.

Testing 

As the project progresses to the testing phase, Egis will ensure that test plans comprehensively cover all technical and functional requirements outlined in the TCC Contracts. Our testing and commissioning experts will witness tests and evaluate results to confirm the system performs as expected and meets relevant standards, ensuring the tolling system meets performance criteria before operational deployment.  

IV Testing Reviewers will assess the implementation of these plans, review the Contractors' records for completeness, and ensure the Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to verify that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been met.

Operational Readiness 

During the operational readiness phase, Egis will ensure that systems, processes, and personnel are fully prepared for tolling operations by assessing the compliance of the TCC Contractors to their management plans and the project’s contractual and operational requirements and ensuring that activities such as user training, support systems and maintenance protocols are in place.  

Capacity and Capability

Please outline your organisation’s knowledge and experience of delivering independent verifier services in the context of Victorian Government procurement processes applied to major projects (particularly transportation infrastructure projects):

Egis has a long track record of successfully delivering transportation infrastructure projects across Australia, including strategic planning, technical assurance and IV. We have extensive knowledge and experience working with Victorian Government clients and have successfully delivered projects for DTP, RSD and MTM, but we have not delivered IV services in Victoria. 

The following projects demonstrate our considerable experience in delivering IV and technical assurance services for various Australian state government agencies: 

Regional Rail Project Independent Certifier, Australia (2019 - current)

Egis has partnered with APP Corporation to provide IC services for the NSW Regional Rail Project fleet being delivered by Momentum Trains under a $2.8B public partnership for Transport for NSW. As the IC, we review and verify the design documentation, manufacture, testing and commissioning of the new rolling stock fleet. Our review of verification activities through the design, manufacturing and testing phases culminates in Certification of Acceptance of the rolling stock before the new fleet is placed into service. 

Brisbane Metro Independent Project Verifier (2016 – current)

Egis is the independent project verifier for the Brisbane Metro Vehicle and the Charging Infrastructure of the Brisbane Metro Project. We reviewed and verified the planning documentation, design, manufacture, testing and commissioning the Metro Vehicle and the Charging Infrastructure and ensured that the project is being delivered in accordance with the Design and Build Deed, the Performance Specification and the relevant Australian Design Rules, Disability Access and Performance Based Standards.

Queensland Train Manufacturing Program (QTMP) Independent Certification (2023 – current)

Egis and SYSTRA Australia Pty. Ltd. formed a Joint Venture to deliver the IC Services for the $9.5B Queensland Government funded QTMP. The project shall deliver 65 new passenger trains to operate on the South-East Queensland rail network, and includes the maintenance and stabling facility at Ormeau and a train manufacturing facility at Torbanlea. The role includes review of all design and test documentation, as well as to conduct surveillance and monitoring activities to certify that the Contractor’s Project Documentation and Project activities (e.g. tests) comply with the defined set of contractual requirements.

Queensland New Generation Rollingstock Accessibility Variation Project Independent Certification (2019 – 2024)

Egis provided independent certification for the design and testing of a suite of 14 modifications packages for the New Generation Rollingstock Operational Readiness Program. With a primary focus on the design stage of the project, the project called on our subject matter experts for the verification of interior-toilets, carbody shell, interior-saloon interior and gangways, brakes and heating, ventilation and air-conditioning.

High Capacity Metro Trains (HCMT) Project Technical Assurance, Victoria (2017 – current)

Egis is the technical advisor for the HCMT Project, the $2.3B public-private partnership (PPP) between the Victorian Government and Evolution Rail. Our role covers all aspects of the design and manufacture of the rolling stock, including providing subject matter experts for all train sub-systems and simulators. Our specialist technical capabilities allowed the application of full systems assurance and associated reliability, availability, maintainability and safety activities throughout the delivery phase of the project, as well as testing and commissioning of both the specialist equipment and the systems as a whole.

Please outline your organisation’s knowledge and experience of delivering independent verifier services in the context of complex technology-based business system projects:

Egis has extensive experience in delivering complex, technology-based services both globally and in Australia. By tapping into our global network for specialized expertise and support, we enhance project outcomes as demonstrated with major initiatives like the (Name major project). Relevant projects include:

Roatex Indonesia Toll System (Indonesia); 2024 - current

Egis Indonesia was appointed in early 2024 as an Independent Supervisory Consultant (ISC) for a PPP Project between the Hungarian government, through Roatex, and the Government of Indonesia. The Project will implement the first Multi-Lane Free Flow (MLFF) technology across all toll road sections in Indonesia. As the ISC, Egis will provide monitoring, supervision, reporting, and quality assurance Services to ensure that the Project is delivered in accordance with the defined standards. 

Clark Airport Expansion (Philippines) 

The Clark Airport Expansion Project, started in 2018, included the design, development and construction of a new Passenger Terminal Building (100,000sqm), designed for throughput of 8 million passengers per year. Egis, with its partner DCCD Engineering, was appointed as the Independent Consultant for the engineering, procurement and construction at Clark Airport for the three-year contract. Egis supported the Client with independent review through the project phases, from design review, through construction and procurement of systems and equipment, testing and commissioning of the new terminal and Operational Readiness and Airport Transition of the New Passenger Terminal Building and its landside support facilities.

Manila LRT Line 1 Extension (Philippines)  

Starting in 2015, the LRT Line 1 was extended from Baclaran Station to Niog Station in Bacoor, Cavite, a distance of 11.7 km. Of this length, 10.5 km was to be elevated and 1.2 km at-grade. The integrated LRT 1 has a total length of approximately 32.4 km and is operated and maintained by the Light Rail Manila Corporation.   Egis Rail, as the leader of the ERIGPHI joint venture, provided Independent Consultancy Services to the client, the Department of Transportation (Philippines).

Stony Point Communications Upgrade Project

Egis Omada was selected by MTM as the primary contractor to undertake the signalling design for the Stony Point Communications Upgrade project. The Stony Point line is one of the first rail lines ever to open in Melbourne and is part of the greater-metropolitan commuter rail network. 

North East Link Project (AUSTRALIA); 2021 - Current

Egis Omada has successfully delivered signalling design for the North East Link Project. As part of the rail interface works, the signalling arrangement and systems required modification and upgrades to ensure signalling assets were relocated outside of the proposed tunnel area.  Egis Omada’s scope of work included modification of the existing signalling arrangement, replacement of life-expired geographical interlocking with a new computer-based interlocking and upgrade of existing signal assets.  All signalling design was completed on time, on schedule and on budget to ensure construction work could be undertaken.  

Key Delivery Individual 

As an experienced Program Director, Systems Engineer, Test Engineer and Business Development professional, Richard has extensive analysis, specialist engineering, flight test, software integration and delivery management experience in the defence, telecommunications, financial and transport sectors. He thrives on building and leading teams and processes to consistently deliver solutions on-time and budget in complex and challenging environments. His direct and focussed style is aimed at removing blockers and holding all stakeholders critical to success accountable for their contributions to deliver the desired business outcomes. This is coupled with a strong sense of ownership and accountability, leading by example to create a high-performance culture.

As the Client Lead, Richard will focus on leading the Egis team to deliver IV Services to support STC’s primary objective of delivering an end-to-end solution for the TCC. Richard will focus on working with the stakeholders to set up the processes for:

A culture of trust and respect – building a foundation of trust forms the basis of working towards best-for-project outcomes.

Effective conflict resolution – large, complex technical projects will invariably include several strong personalities with strong opinions. Richard will ensure that his team approaches disagreements constructively and ’plays the ball, not the person’ to ensure an enduring positive working relationship. 

Role clarity – Richard will work with the parties to ensure that roles and responsibilities are clear early, to avoid any confusion or items ’falling through the cracks’ during the life of the project.

Effective escalation and resolution – Every project will experience issues. It is how they are resolved that will determine success. Richard will support the development of effective governance, and risk and issues resolution processes to enable speedy resolution, thereby promoting schedule adherence.

Richard’s CV (attached) provides detail regarding his experience and qualifications, and will bring his experience from the following relevant projects: 

Egis - Principal Consultant, M6 OMCS Project (2024)

Downer – General Manager, Systems Integration (2023 – 2024)

Downer – Technical Director, HCMT (2023)

Downer – Systems Engineering Manager (2022 – 2023)

Downer - GM Engineering (2017 – 2022)

Richard will begin the engagement at the required capacity to ensure that the Egis team is effectively onboarded and that the required interfaces are set up with the STC and TCC Contractor personnel and processes. Richard’s engagement will then phase down to that required for effective oversight of the team, regular reporting and communication with the STC and Project stakeholders and the resolution of any issues.

Risk Management

Please provide sufficient evidence and experience from similar projects to demonstrate an understanding of the risks, issues and opportunities that commonly arise and how the identified risks were managed:

Egis Oceania has extensive experience managing commercial and project risk for our public and private sector clients. Egis Oceania's capabilities include the identification and quantification of infrastructure project related risks including design, construction and commissioning risk; operational risk; market risk; network and interface risk; industrial relations risk; and asset ownership risk (including residual risk). We are also familiar with the mechanisms of risk transfer and the role of risk allocation and value-for-money in tender evaluations. The generic structure of our risk management processes are aligned with AS/NZS 31000 2009: Risk Management.  At appropriate stages in complex projects, we facilitate risk management workshops (using an established methodology, an agreed risk register template and an agreed scale of likelihoods, impacts and consequences). Risk Management workshops will focus on areas of risk relevant to the particular project including: commercial risk, service delivery risk, reputational risk, project timing, technical quality and stakeholder relationships. For each new engagement, following the project inception meeting Egis will facilitate a risk management workshop with the relevant Project Stakeholders to establish the initial risk register and rate the risks using the scale of likelihoods, impacts and consequences, and with risk owners identified and with defined risk mitigation strategies.  

Identified risks will be assessed as to their priority to be managed. 

Egis have successfully delivered similar services, such as QTMP IC, we did this with our tried-and-true Risk Based Approach (RBA). As we are on QTMP, Egis will undertake a high-level assessment to rank identified risks associated with each Project and Design requirement in terms of consequence and likelihood. This will determine the level and type of review needed for each requirement and support a robust and repeatable evidence-based assessment across all requirements. Requirements defined as medium and high risk (see figure x) will be subject to a more intensive level of compliance assessment. This rating process is critical to form the basis for the design reviews, certification of design packages and identification/resolution of Potential, Actual and Minor Non-Compliances. 

If the Key Stakeholders disagree with the level of risk associated with a design requirement and the level of compliance assessment effort to be applied, our IV team will work collaboratively with those organisations to align/agree the risk allocation. If the level of risk associated with any requirement is unclear, a more conservative view will be taken i.e. a higher risk ranking will be assigned, and our team will apply the commensurate level of effort in our review and assessment. 

Egis will assess and rate the risks associated with each design package to determine the level of rigour we will apply in the certification process for each package and in monitoring controls that are applied. This supports an agile and efficient approach to compliance assessment, targeting allocation of our resources to ensure the level of effort and type of assessment is proportionate to the risk associated with a particular design package or deliverable, in achieving the objectives of the Project. 

Quality Management Systems

Our ISO:9001-certified Quality Management Systems (QMS) are built on a foundation of clear scope, project execution plans, regular project meetings, task breakdowns, and budgets for each project team. We ensure quality through peer reviews of all deliverables, monthly internal reviews with the Egis Project Director, and external reporting to our clients.  

Project managers are responsible for embedding Quality Assurance (QA) into the project workflow, including resource allocation, scheduling QA activities, and conducting design reviews at critical stages to verify calculations, assumptions, and compliance with specifications. As projects are dynamic and changes are inevitable, effective change management is a key factor in our success. We ensure that changes and risks are communicated regularly and promptly, enhancing stakeholder engagement and facilitating proactive issue resolution. This approach allows us to update project plans and baselines, ensuring potential impacts are addressed swiftly and supporting on-time delivery and project success.  

We understand that the quality management process must align with the customer or stakeholder’s needs. This helps define the required quality management processes and performance measurements. Our focus is on maintaining quality consistency throughout the project while remaining flexible and agile to meet shifting demands. Ultimately, our project quality management approach ensures that the project meets its intended objectives and delivers customer satisfaction. 

Examples of the ways in which Egis will work to achieve the best possible fitness for purpose on our clients’ projects include: 

Taking time to understand the underlying project drivers and critical issues that will make the project a success for our clients. 

Proactively scheduling and making time for opportunities for our clients to provide feedback on our work and for contractors, partners, and other consultants to provide their own comments and input. 

Issuing draft documents and work in progress (WIP) drawings/models and actively seeking and taking onboard feedback so we can contribute towards achieving overall project objectives. 

Taking a collaborative approach to reviews ensures that the process enhances the overall outcomes. 

Working collaboratively with our clients’ teams and project delivery partners using digital platforms and environments.  Our project quality management consists of three major processes:                                                                      

Quality Management Planning: Our quality planning focuses on taking all the information available at the beginning of the project and resolving how we will measure quality, establish KPIs, and prevent rework. This involves identifying the quality requirements and standards required for our projects. The project quality management process is clearly shared with all stakeholders, and appropriate tasks are delegated to those responsible to ensure the required outcomes.                                                                                                             

Quality Control: This involves ascertaining the review, approval requirements for the validation and verification of all deliverables prior to issuing to the client.                                                                                

Quality Assurance: This involves monitoring, auditing, and recording the results of quality activities to assess performance and recommend and implement necessary changes. Egis views effective quality management as a tool to increase competitiveness and performance and ensure constant change and improvement.

Are the quality systems certified?    No

If the answer to the above is ‘Yes’, what Australian or International standards apply:

Egis Oceania operates under an integrated HSEQ management system that consists of the following comprehensive third-party accredited system elements: Quality Management System, complying with ISO 9001 Environmental Management System, complying with ISO 14001 Occupational Health & Safety Management System, complying with AS/NZS 4801.

Process methodologies

Please outline your organisation’s experience of delivering independent verifier services under Victorian Government procurement processes with respect to ensuring a product, system or service complies with Requirements and Deliverables:

Internal systems and processes Egis utilises to deliver our projects to time, scope and budget include:

Nominated project management team: The project management team organises and prepares the contract execution plan, including rights and obligations, key milestones, services and deliverables, input data to be collected, applicable regulations and standards, communications plan, risks and opportunities, health and safety, corporate social responsibility, and ethics. They also ensure project objectives are met, track performance, and build team morale. Project Directors, Project Managers, and Commercial Managers are responsible for leading teams, managing resources, and ensuring that learning is transferred across projects.

Financial management: The project manager utilises a bottom-up budgeting tool called Project Toolbox, which is used for project scoping and pricing. This tool provides a detailed breakdown of all costs to be incurred on the project, enabling the tracking of tasks and budgets. 

Work package brief: This is a document recording the scope and inputs/outputs for specific project tasks with budget allocation and expected timeframes and quality assurance requirements.

Discipline-specific program: Programs are completed for each stage of the work and aligned with the master program.

Project issues register: This repository is used for recording the project issues, updated weekly, and then used to inform progress reports. 

Contract progress reports: We provide regular progress reporting to our clients and team to report on work completed, proposed work for the next period, any new risks and issues and further information required.

Project meetings: Internal project meetings are used to discuss progress, work accomplished, planned work, technical issues, and potential scope changes, as well as to identify any risks or problems that could impact project delivery. Project Managers and relevant line managers discuss conflicts regarding resourcing and project priorities. 

Internal reviews: We perform staged and timely internal project reviews to minimise the risk of re-work and ensure that an appropriate level of technical expertise is assigned at the project's outset.  

Please outline your organisation’s familiarity with and direct experience of providing independent verifier services for projects managed in accordance with the Project Development and Construction Management Act 1994 (Vic)(public construction):

Past performance and current work

Proven methodology

Egis has a proven track record and significant experience (XX+ years) delivering IV services on major transport projects in Australia and internationally.

Egis has a developed methodology for successfully delivering IV services. Our approach is based on a proven methodology that has consistently delivered results across multiple high-profile projects. This methodology incorporates best practices, robust tools, and lessons learned from comparable initiatives.

Egis has a solid foundation in managing IV specific document management systems, automated review and certification workflows, as well as advanced reporting and surveillance tools. These capabilities ensure greater efficiency and cost-effective delivery of IV services for NEL.

Our deep experience in both project delivery and IV equips us with a comprehensive understanding of the required services, the design approval process, and the complexities involved in addressing multiple stakeholder requirements on complex tolling projects. 

The below are the four key features which define the Egis certification approach:

Structured and Robust approach.  We will articulate a clear, specific, and logical process for certification that is repeatable across all design packages, construction milestones and completion procedures. Over the course of a long program of work, this consistency will allow all parties to understand what is expected and tailor their work methods to suit. 

Risk-based and appropriately resourced. We will ensure appropriate resourcing for the specific tasks at hand.  Each assessment will be made objectively with effort required to be proportionate to the risk associated if the task is not completed.

Collaborative yet independent. We will work transparently with all stakeholders (through continual and proactive dialogue; objectivity, and informal assistance with early issues identification and resolution). In doing so, it, will ensure it remains independent, consistent, and non-biased throughout the certification process. Effective collaboration between project stakeholders will be critical to the success of the overall project. Egis will implement a collaborative culture and facilitate opportunities to discuss solutions across various packages. This will be achieved through:

Active and collaborative problem solving.

Formal and informal dialogue.

A culture of sharing knowledge and information e.g. results of any on-site or off-site inspection, defect reporting, testing and audits regarding quality or compliance including any actual or potential non-compliance; An attitude of connected team, rather than ‘us’ and ‘them’ to foster an effective and efficient working behaviour Ensuring ownership of the project delivery remains with the delivery contractors while the IV team has the mechanism with which it can provide independent scrutiny across the design delivery process. The cohesive working environment will enhance confidence by delivery contractors in the IV process and vice versa.

Evidence-based certification methodology.  We will ensure that an evidence-based approach is used to test our work, prior to an IV review and certification occurring.

Reporting

A core requirement of efficiently delivering these aspects of the IV services is an accurate single source of truth, with Quality processes embedded into the workflows managed by online tools and systems. As well as managing workflows and the significant volume of documents associated with the IV services. This will inform key deliverables like the Progress Report to the Project stakeholders. 

For example, our central comments register created by Power BI can be analysed in terms of progress against key metrics, with the performance data visualised in a dashboard for tracking and reporting. 

Improvement

Over the life of the IV services and NEL, Egis is committed to continuous improvement and seeking opportunities for innovation. As new technology or systems become available that provide benefits and efficiencies in delivery of IV services, Egis will consider opportunities for automation of key tasks (e.g. reviewing design packages, managing/closing out comments) and potential use of artificial intelligence. If new digital tools and systems are fit for our purpose and offer efficiency benefits to the IV team, we will introduce them with the appropriate level of assurance, as part of a shared learning journey.

Social Procurement

Indirect Expenditure via Social Benefit Suppliers

Egis is committed to supporting Indigenous entrepreneurship and business development. We actively prioritise engaging with Indigenous and Torres Strait Islander businesses, particularly in indirect expenditure categories such as office supplies, catering, cleaning, training, and printing. This approach not only contributes to the economic success of Indigenous communities but also creates long-term social benefits.

We:

Prioritise purchasing from Indigenous enterprises where possible, including sourcing PPE from SupplyAus Holdings, stationary from Gulbari, and publishing/printing services from Iscariot Media.

Partner with organisations like Deadly Coders and offer Cultural Awareness Training delivered by First Nations trainers.

Work with Supply Nation to procure office supplies and IT equipment from verified Indigenous-owned businesses.

These initiatives align with our broader commitment to our Reconciliation Action Plan (RAP), fostering relationships with First Nations communities and businesses. By continuing to engage with Indigenous suppliers, we support their growth and provide meaningful opportunities for economic participation. Should we be successful in the North East Link project, we will further expand our engagement with local First Nations suppliers, further strengthening the Indigenous business community in Victoria.

Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) Strategy and Gender Inclusive Policy

Egis is committed to fostering a diverse and inclusive workplace. Our DEI strategy, focused on First Nations, Disability, Gender, Rainbow, and Culture, aims to create an environment where all employees can thrive.

Our gender inclusivity initiatives include:

Aiming to increase female representation across the workforce from 31.3% to 33% and leadership from 25.2% to 27% by 2025.

Addressing the gender pay gap and promoting career development for women.

Supporting families through a strong parental leave policy that provides flexibility.

We actively implement DEI initiatives through our employee-led DEI Network, which drives events such as International Women’s Day and NAIDOC Week. Egis is also compliant with the Australian Workplace Gender Equality Act, and we regularly monitor our progress towards closing gender gaps and promoting diversity at all levels. Our efforts ensure an inclusive workplace that values equality, creating opportunities for all employees to succeed and contribute to a high-performance culture.
