6 COMPLIANCE WITH REQUIREMENTS

6.1 Our Understanding of Services
The State Tolling Corporation (STC) has proposed to develop an end-to-end solution for the Toll Collection
Capability (TCC) that incorporates the delivery and operation of a Roadside System (RSS) and the delivery,
support, and maintenance of a Back-Office system (BOS).




FIGURE 1 - PHASES

PROGRAM SERVICES
Egis will submit an Independent Verifier (IV) Plan (please see draft in Attachment 2) within 20 business days
of commencement. This plan will be agreed with STC and will detail:

▬ Skills, expertise and experience of the resources and the estimated resource levels required,
▬ Progress reports to be provided to the Project Control Group (PCG), and
▬ A verification audit program to monitor performance of the Contractors’ obligations under the TCC.

REQUIREMENTS PHASE SERVICES
We will provide STC with an independent, expert opinion on whether the specified technical and business
requirements— including the Scope of Works and Technical Requirements (SWTRs)— have been accurately
translated into robust, verifiable requirements.
We will ensure that TCC Contractors implement strong processes to capture specialist engineering
requirements, such as safety, human factors, Reliability, Availability and Maintainability (RAM), and cyber
security. These requirements will complement the SWTRs and are typically gathered through workshops with
subject matter experts from the operational community.
All technical requirements must be captured in a centralised repository that serves as the single source of
truth and align with the International Council on Systems Engineering (INCOSE) standards. If the project uses
a Requirements Management Database (RMDB) such as IBM DOORS, we can provide specialist resources to
set up the RMDB and develop templates and tools for tracking and managing requirements. Additionally, we
can offer training for both STC and TCC Contractor staff on how to use these tools effectively.
We will review the Requirements Verification Traceability Matrices (RVTMs) to ensure that verification
evidence is captured at each stage of the project lifecycle. This will provide early assurance that all
requirements have been adequately verified and highlight any gaps or 'orphans' that need to be addressed.




PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                              3/36
DESIGN PHASE SERVICES
We will conduct document reviews for each of the TCC Contract design deliverables in accordance with the
Project Delivery Schedule and will provide structured feedback for items that do not meet the specified
requirements.
Egis will also advise STC when each deliverable is suitable for endorsement or acceptance under the terms of
the TCC Contracts.

TEST PHASE SERVICES
We will provide specialist staff to witness specified tests and demonstrations, ensuring that the requirements
needing verification through these methods are satisfactorily met.
Additionally, we will provide ongoing updates on the maturity of the RVTMs and offer advice on when the
Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to confirm that the requirements
within the TCC Contracts have been fulfilled.

IMPLEMENTATION AND OPERATIONAL READINESS PHASE SERVICES
Operational readiness is typically the responsibility of the Project Integrator, working with the Operator. Egis
will tap into our experience in previous projects to support the operational readiness planning and ensure
that the transition from Project to Operations happens seamlessly.


6.2 Our Approach to Test Witnessing
Egis conducts all test witnessing activities with a clearly defined set of objectives, which includes:

▬ The verification of test results,
▬ Assurance of compliance,
▬ Ensuring documentation traceability, and
▬ Identification & mitigation of risks.
We conduct thorough technical reviews of test plans, schedules, and performance or functional
requirements. These reviews help identify critical test cases, potential compliance issues, and operational
deficiencies, enabling us to provide constructive feedback. We will develop a test witness schedule focused
on these critical test cases to ensure that suitably experienced technical witnesses are present as needed.
Test witnessing observations are systematically collected and categorised according to the established
objectives, then communicated concisely to the project. Responses, resulting controls, and any changes to
test plans will be tracked to ensure risk mitigation (more on risk can be found in Section 8) and closure of
observations.
Egis will coordinate closely with the project team to ensure comments and observations are directed to the
relevant forums and escalation levels. Our approach is adaptable, and we will tailor the process to best
support the project by adding or removing scope based on stakeholder requirements, or adjusting outputs
to align with existing project systems


6.3 Approach to GORC and its Application
Egis will implement a structured and proactive approach to General Overview and Reasonable Checking
(GORC) throughout all stages of the project, ensuring full compliance with the technical, assurance, and
contractual requirements set out in the TCC Contracts. The IV team will be led by a dedicated management


PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                               4/36
team, with experience applying GORC practices on major Victorian transport projects such as the High
Capacity Metro Trains (HCMT) and X’Trapolis 2 (XT2) Technical advisor roles. Egis’ approach is to provide
continuous oversight, identify potential issues early, and resolve them promptly, minimizing risks and
ensuring the successful deployment of the tolling system.
The IV Plan, along with supporting procedures, will outline methodologies for meeting key performance and
traceability requirements. Project risks will be organised by discipline, with risk ratings providing guidance for
resourcing efforts. This approach will help prioritize key aspects of the project and determine the necessary
actions as outlined for the QTMP IC project in Section 8. These ratings will be reviewed and adjusted as the
project evolves by the IC management team in consultation with STC representatives.
A Completion Plan will be developed in line with the Contractor’s documents which outlines the information
required for the IV to make progressive assessments of each Critical Interface Milestone. Regular progress
reports, governance meetings and audits will inform decision-making and enable prompt resolution of
issues. Close communication with the STC and all stakeholders along with updates to the Services Delivery
Management Plan on a 6 monthly basis will ensure alignment and facilitate early intervention when
necessary.

MANAGEMENT PLANS, REQUIREMENTS, AND DESIGN DOCUMENTS
During the requirements and design review stage of the project, Egis will review the TCC Contractors’
management plans, including technical specifications, quality assurance strategies, risk management plans
and schedules. This will ensure that these plans align with the TCC Contracts and provide a realistic
foundation for successful project delivery.
We will assess the consistency of these documents with broader NEL tollway objectives, ensuring that they
comply with legal, regulatory, and contractual requirements, tapping into Egis’ international expertise as
required.

TESTING
As the project progresses to the testing phase, Egis will ensure that test plans comprehensively cover all
technical and functional requirements outlined in the TCC Contracts. Our testing and commissioning experts
will witness tests and evaluate results to confirm the system performs as expected and meets relevant
standards, ensuring the tolling system meets performance criteria before operational deployment.
IV Testing Reviewers will assess the implementation of these plans, review the Contractors' records for
completeness, and ensure the Project RVTM is complete, accurate, and contains the necessary evidence to
verify that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been met.

OPERATIONAL READINESS
During the operational readiness phase, Egis will ensure that systems, processes, and personnel are fully
prepared for tolling operations by assessing the compliance of the TCC Contractors to their management
plans and the project’s contractual and operational requirements and ensuring that activities such as user
training, support systems and maintenance protocols are in place.

projects demonstrate our considerable experience in delivering IV and technical assurance services for
various Australian state government agencies.

REGIONAL RAIL PROJECT – INDEPENDENT CERTIFIER (2019 – CURRENT)

                                     Rail Project fleet being delivered by Momentum Trains under a $2.8B
                                     public partnership for Transport for NSW. As the IC, we review and verify
                                     the design documentation, manufacture, testing and commissioning of
                                     the new rolling stock fleet. Our review of verification activities through
                                     the design, manufacturing and testing phases culminates in Certification
of Acceptance of the rolling stock before the new fleet is placed into service.

Egis is the independent project verifier for the Brisbane Metro Vehicle
and the Charging Infrastructure of the Brisbane Metro Project. We
reviewed and verified the planning documentation, design,
manufacture, testing and commissioning the Metro Vehicle and the
Charging Infrastructure and ensured that the project is being
delivered in accordance with the Design and Build Deed, the
Performance Specification and the relevant Australian Design Rules, Disability Access and Performance Based
Standards.

8 RISK MANAGEMENT

8.1 Risks, Issues and Opportunities
We understand that successful project delivery requires effective risk management, prompt issue resolution,
and the identification of opportunities for continuous improvement. With our extensive experience in
managing complex projects, including infrastructure and tolling systems across Australia and the Asia-Pacific
region, we bring a risk-based approach (RBA) to every stage of the project, as we have on similar projects
such as QTMP (see Table 6 6 for example of identified risks, issues and opportunities).
TABLE 6 6 - RISKS, ISSUES, OPPORTUNITIES

 Project       Risk                           Issue                           Opportunity
 QTMP          Delays caused by the           Project risk that required      Build a competency framework
               main Contractors               program recovery is not         which can call on international

PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                                14/36
RISKS AND ISSUES




FIGURE 4 - TYPICAL RISKS AND ISSUES
Our approach includes identifying and quantifying risks and issues across relevant disciplines and phases and
include design, construction, testing, commissioning, operations, market, network, industrial relations, and
asset ownership. We follow the AS/NZS 31000:2018 Risk Management framework, ensuring that
management processes are structured and effective.
Risk and issue management as an IV includes managing risks inherent in delivering IV services and
importantly, ensuring that the processes are in place to adequately solicit and manage to conclusion, the
client’s and Contractors’ risks which could impact successful project delivery. Risks we typically manage as an
IV include, but are not limited to:

▬ Unclear expectations of the IV services to be provided, impacting confidence.
▬ The impact of poor designs being rejected and impacting the project schedule.
▬ Suitable client resources being unavailable to support the defined IV processes, impacting the project
  schedule.
▬ Stakeholders have differing opinions regarding levels of compliance with requirements.
Our RBA starts with clear communication and risk management workshops. These workshops use a defined
methodology, risk registers, and a scale for assessing risk likelihood, impact, and consequence. At project
inception, we facilitate a workshop to establish the initial risk register, prioritise risks, assign owners, and
define mitigation strategies. Higher-risk items are given higher priority for mitigation. If stakeholders
disagree on risk levels, we collaborate to reach alignment, taking a more conservative approach when
necessary. Our extensive experience in similar projects enables us to effectively manage risks and apply these
insights to the NEL project.
Egis employs a pragmatic and proactive approach to monitoring project risks that are realised, ensuring
these are captured and categorised appropriately. We have applied this approach to numerous projects
including the VSBA Cobblebank and Moorabbin projects, by prioritising issues by impact and urgency.




PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                            15/36
OPPORTUNITIES




FIGURE 5 - OPPORTUNITIES

Opportunities for innovation, process improvement and technology upgrades are regularly updated and
monitored throughout the duration of the project. Egis’ experience with similar projects around the globe
provides a wealth of knowledge to draw upon when offering up opportunities for schedule, sustainability,
technical and various other improvements.


8.2 Quality Management Systems
Our ISO:9001-certified Quality Management Systems (QMS) are built on a foundation of clear scope, project
execution plans, regular project meetings, task breakdowns, and budgets for each project team. We ensure
quality through peer reviews of all deliverables, monthly internal reviews with the Egis Project Director, and
external reporting to our clients.
Project managers are responsible for embedding Quality Assurance (QA) into the project workflow, including
resource allocation, scheduling QA activities, and conducting design reviews at critical stages to verify
calculations, assumptions, and compliance with specifications. As projects are dynamic and changes are
inevitable, effective change management is a key factor in our success. We ensure that changes and risks are
communicated regularly and promptly, enhancing stakeholder engagement and facilitating proactive issue
resolution. This approach allows us to update project plans and baselines, ensuring potential impacts are
addressed swiftly and supporting on-time delivery and project success.
We understand that the quality management process must align with the customer or stakeholder’s needs.
This helps define the required quality management processes and performance measurements. Our focus is
on maintaining quality consistency throughout the project while remaining flexible and agile to meet shifting
demands. Ultimately, our project quality management approach ensures that the project meets its intended
objectives and delivers customer satisfaction.
Examples of the ways in which Egis will work to achieve the best possible fitness for purpose on our clients’
projects include:

▬ Taking time to understand the underlying project drivers and critical issues that will make the project a
  success for our clients.
▬ Proactively scheduling and making time for opportunities for our clients to provide feedback on our work
  and for contractors, partners, and other consultants to provide their own comments and input.



PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                            16/36
           ▬ Issuing draft documents and work in progress (WIP) drawings/models and actively seeking and taking
             onboard feedback so we can contribute towards achieving overall project objectives.
           ▬ Taking a collaborative approach to reviews ensures that the process enhances the overall outcomes.
           ▬ Working collaboratively with our clients’ teams and project delivery partners using digital platforms and
             environments. Our project quality management consists of three major processes:
               ▬ Quality Management Planning: Our quality planning focuses on taking all the information available
                 at the beginning of the project and resolving how we will measure quality, establish KPIs, and prevent
                 rework. This involves identifying the quality requirements and standards required for our projects. The
                 project quality management process is clearly shared with all stakeholders, and appropriate tasks are
                 delegated to those responsible to ensure the required outcomes.
               ▬ Quality Control: This involves ascertaining the review, approval requirements for the validation and
                 verification of all deliverables prior to issuing to the client.
               ▬ Quality Assurance: This involves monitoring, auditing, and recording the results of quality activities to
                 assess performance and recommend and implement necessary changes. Egis views effective quality
                 management as a tool to increase competitiveness and performance and ensure constant change and
                 improvement.

the performance data visualised in a dashboard for tracking and reporting.

CONTINUOUS IMPROVEMENT
Over the life of the IV services and NEL, Egis is committed to continuous improvement and seeking
opportunities for innovation. As new technology or systems become available that provide benefits and
efficiencies in delivery of IV services, Egis will embrace opportunities for automation of key tasks (e.g.
reviewing design packages, managing/closing out comments). If new digital tools and systems are fit for our
purpose and offer efficiency benefits to the IV team, we will introduce them with the appropriate level of
assurance, as part of a shared learning journey.


9.2 Demonstrated Experience in Providing Independent Verifier Services for
    Projects Under the Project Development and Construction Management Act
    1994 (Vic)
Egis has extensive experience delivering large, complex projects for State Government departments and
entities in Victoria, particularly in the public transport, education, and infrastructure sectors. Our role has
typically involved acting as the State’s Technical Advisor, Project Manager, Superintendent, or Contract
Administrator, where we have been responsible for overseeing high-value, high-risk capital projects. These
include the procurement of new fleet assets, transport infrastructure, and public sector building projects,
where we have applied various procurement strategies, such as lump sum contracts, design and construct
contracts, and PPP transactions.

Our work has been conducted within the framework of the Project Development and Construction
Management Act 1994 (Vic), which governs public construction projects in the state. We have significant
familiarity with this Act, particularly in relation to the Ministerial Directions that guide public construction
procurement. Egis has a strong understanding of these Directions and has consistently ensured compliance
with them when delivering capital projects.

We are well-versed in managing government-funded procurement processes, including:

▬ Implementing transparent, defined tender processes that ensure fair engagement with the market and the
  selection of qualified consultants and contractors.
▬ Ensuring confidentiality of project documentation, managing conflicts of interest, and maintaining probity
  throughout the tender process.
▬ Applying Ministerial Directions and complying with the Victorian State Government Supplier Code of
  Conduct and the Social Procurement Framework to promote ethical, sustainable, and socially responsible
  procurement.
▬ Assessing and resolving claims and disputes relating to design, scope, time, cost, quality, and compliance
  in an impartial manner.



PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                              19/36
▬ Maintaining a comprehensive understanding of project status, risks, and issues to support timely decision-
  making throughout the project lifecycle.
▬ Managing the engagement of specialist consultants and ensuring all technical aspects of a project are
  compliant with required standards.
▬ Ensuring strict project governance, adherence to delegations and authority, and clear communication with
  the Project Control Group.
▬ Aligning services, management plans, and systems with the Department or Agency’s requirements.
Examples of Egis’s experience relevant to the role of an Independent Verifier include:

▬ For the HCMT PPP, Egis conducted testing and commissioning of trains to confirm compliance with
  operational and performance standards.
▬ For HCMT and the XTrapolis 2.0 Train Fleet, Egis personnel were seconded offshore to monitor the
  manufacturing process of critical carriage body components, ensuring compliance with quality standards
  before components were shipped to Australia.
▬ As Project Manager for the Department of Justice, Egis oversaw the replacement of the Duress Alarm
  System at Melbourne Assessment Prison, including facilitating a test of the proposed system under real-
  world conditions to confirm it met operational requirements.
▬ During the New Schools PPP, Egis worked with the Independent Certifier to verify the completion of
  multiple schools, ensuring all elements met required standards and were ready for operation in time for
  the new school year.


10 PAST PERFORMANCE AND CURRENT WORK

10.1 Proven Methodology
Egis has a proven track record and significant experience delivering IV services on major transport projects in
Australia and internationally. Our approach is based on a proven methodology that has consistently delivered
results across multiple high-profile projects around Australia. This methodology incorporates best practices,
robust tools, and lessons learned from comparable initiatives.

Egis has a solid foundation in managing IV specific document management systems, automated review and
certification workflows, as well as advanced reporting and surveillance tools. These capabilities ensure greater
efficiency and cost-effective delivery of IV services for NEL.

Our deep experience in both project delivery and IV equips us with a comprehensive understanding of the
required services, the design approval process, and the complexities involved in addressing multiple
stakeholder requirements on complex tolling projects.
The below are the four key features which define the Egis certification approach:




PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                           20/36
FIGURE 7 - PROVEN METHODOLOGY


▬ Structured and Robust approach. We will articulate a clear, specific, and logical process for certification
  that is repeatable across all design packages, construction milestones and completion procedures. Over
  the course of a long program of work, this consistency will allow all parties to understand what is
  expected and tailor their work methods to suit.
▬ Risk-based and appropriately resourced. We will ensure appropriate resourcing for the specific tasks at
  hand. Each assessment will be made objectively with effort required to be proportionate to the risk
  associated if the task is not completed.
▬ Collaborative yet independent. We will work transparently with all stakeholders (through continual and
  proactive dialogue; objectivity, and informal assistance with early issues identification and resolution). In
  doing so, it, will ensure it remains independent, consistent, and non-biased throughout the certification
  process. Effective collaboration between project stakeholders will be critical to the success of the overall
  project. Egis will implement a collaborative culture and facilitate opportunities to discuss solutions across
  various packages. This will be achieved through:
   ▬ Active and collaborative problem solving.
   ▬ Formal and informal dialogue.
   ▬ A culture of sharing knowledge and information e.g. results of any on-site or off-site inspection,
     defect reporting, testing and audits regarding quality or compliance including any actual or potential
     non-compliance; An attitude of connected team, rather than ‘us’ and ‘them’ to foster an effective and
     efficient working behaviour Ensuring ownership of the project delivery remains with the delivery
     contractors while the IV team has the mechanism with which it can provide independent scrutiny
     across the design delivery process. The cohesive working environment will enhance confidence by
     delivery contractors in the IV process and vice versa.
▬ Evidence-based certification methodology. We will ensure that an evidence-based approach is used to
  test our work, prior to an IV review and certification occurring.
While there are fundamental differences between the delivery of works packages and their associated third
parties, our approach and methodology to deliver the IV services will be consistent across all packages (see
Figure 8 below).




PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                           21/36
FIGURE 8 - PROJECT PHASES


10.2 Case Study
Egis and CBS have been delivering tolling projects around the world, including MCX Toll Collection System
(TCS) Upgrade in Philippines, A2 motorway in European and Roatex toll system in Indonesia. Our local team,
with the assistance of our global experts will bring a deep understanding of the tolling system and the needs
of the NEL.

WESTERN HARBOUR TUNNEL (WHT) TOLLING PROJECT – TFNSW

Transport for NSW (TfNSW) | 2023 - Current
                                 Value: Not disclosed
                                 Program: WHT Tolling Project, TfNSW
                                 Scope: Definition, procurement, test and implementation of the roadside
                                 and back-office tolling systems for the new Western Harbour Tunnel (WHT),
                                 Sydney.


Project Overview
The Western Harbour Tunnel project is a major infrastructure initiative in Sydney, Australia, designed to
improve transport efficiency by providing a third harbour crossing. The project includes a 6.5-kilometer tolled
twin-tunnel connecting Rozelle to Waverton, easing congestion on the Sydney Harbour Bridge, Sydney
Harbour Tunnel, and ANZAC Bridge. Once completed, it will enhance connectivity, reduce travel times, and
support Sydney’s growing population and economy.




PROCUREMENT OF INDEPENDENT VERIFIER SERVICES – NORTH EAST LINK
                                                                                                            22/36
Role
The procurement for WHT Tolling is at tender stage with responses due around mid-2025. The team has led
the procurement including Specification development, market interactives, contract documentation including
commercial framework, payment mechanism and KPI regime, whole of life budget development, and tender
evaluation. This role is ongoing throughout the procurement and implementation phases of the project.
Impacts and Benefits:
▬ End-to-end system review of the toll data collection and processing;
▬ Integrated test and verification of the system;
▬ Assessment of whole-of-life impacts as part of reviews;
▬ Improved commercial framework for tolling provider engagement;
▬ Rigorous documentation for transparency and auditability.

M6 TUNNEL TOLLING PROJECT – TFNSW

Transport for NSW (TfNSW) | 2023 - Current
                                Value: Not disclosed
                                Program: M6 Tolling Project, TfNSW
                                Scope: Definition, procurement, test and implementation of the roadside and
                                back-office tolling systems for the new M6 Tunnel, Sydney.




Project Overview
The M6 Stage 1 project is a critical transport infrastructure development in Sydney, extending the M8
motorway by 4 kilometres to Kogarah. This project aims to reduce traffic congestion, improve travel times,
and enhance connectivity for southern Sydney by providing a direct underground link to the city’s motorway
network. Once completed, it will support efficient freight movement, reduce pressure on local roads, and
contribute to Sydney’s economic growth.

Role
The procurement for M6 Stage 1 Tolling is at pre-tender stage. Similarly to WHT Tolling project, CBS is leading
the procurement including specification development, market interactives, contract documentation including
commercial framework, payment mechanism and KPI regime, whole of life budget development, and tender
evaluation. CBS’s role will be ongoing throughout the procurement and implementation phases of the project.
Impacts and Benefits:
▬ End-to-end system review of the toll data collection and processing;
▬ Integrated test and verification of the system;
▬ Assessment of whole-of-life impacts as part of reviews;
▬ Improved commercial framework for tolling provider engagement;

Pricing is based on matching a mix of SME resources to best suit the respective packages, used flexibly to
increase / decrease / respond to specific STC requests. Given that the scope of services is very dependent on
the level of documentation provided by the RSS and BOS contractors, we propose the following commercial
arrangement.
▬ We have provided an indicative Target Outturn Fee from commencement in March 2025 to completion in
      June 20291, in 2025 dollars.
▬ The Target Outturn Fee has been based on a Schedule of Rates for each resource and estimated hours
      per resource, also based on the number of packages – 14 Simple, 9 Medium and 1 Complex.
▬ Egis will conduct two review cycles per package.
▬ STC review comments will be consolidated by STC before submission to Egis.
▬ Test witnessing will be in person in Melbourne, or online if interstate or overseas.
▬ Services will be provided on a Schedule of Rates basis, plus any disbursements at-cost plus 10%.
▬ At the end of each quarter, we will review the actual costs expended and re-estimate the fees for the next
      quarter, for approval.
▬ At the end of each calendar year, we will adjust the Rates, based on verifiable CPI, or WPI information.
▬ Rates for local resources (Melbourne based) are based on Egis’ Vendorpanel profile. Egis SME rates are
      based on offshore rates used previously for Transport contracts (these rates are lower than the
      Vendorpanel rates).

12 SOCIAL PROCUREMENT

12.1 Indirect Expenditure via Social Benefit Suppliers
Egis is committed to supporting Indigenous entrepreneurship and business development. We actively
prioritise engaging with Indigenous and Torres Strait Islander businesses, particularly in indirect expenditure
categories such as office supplies, catering, cleaning, training, and printing. This approach not only
contributes to the economic success of Indigenous communities but also creates long-term social benefits.
We:

▬ Prioritise purchasing from Indigenous enterprises where possible, including sourcing PPE from SupplyAus
  Holdings, stationary from Gulbari, and publishing/printing services from Iscariot Media.
▬ Partner with organisations like Deadly Coders and offer Cultural Awareness Training delivered by First
  Nations trainers.
▬ Work with Supply Nation to procure office supplies and IT equipment from verified Indigenous-owned
  businesses.
These initiatives align with our broader commitment to our Reconciliation Action Plan (RAP), fostering
relationships with First Nations communities and businesses. By continuing to engage with Indigenous
suppliers, we support their growth and provide meaningful opportunities for economic participation. Should
we be successful in the North East Link project, we will further expand our engagement with local First
Nations suppliers, further strengthening the Indigenous business community in Victoria.


12.2 Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) Strategy and Gender Inclusive Policy
Egis is committed to fostering a diverse and inclusive workplace. Our DEI strategy, focused on First Nations,
Disability, Gender, Rainbow, and Culture, aims to create an environment where all employees can thrive.
Our gender inclusivity initiatives include:

▬ Aiming to increase female representation across the workforce from 31.3% to 33% and leadership from
  25.2% to 27% by 2025.
▬ Addressing the gender pay gap and promoting career development for women.
▬ Supporting families through a strong parental leave policy that provides flexibility.
We actively implement DEI initiatives through our employee-led DEI Network, which drives events such as
International Women’s Day and NAIDOC Week. Egis is also compliant with the Australian Workplace Gender
Equality Act, and we regularly monitor our progress towards closing gender gaps and promoting diversity at
all levels. Our efforts ensure an inclusive workplace that values equality, creating opportunities for all
employees to succeed and contribute to a high-performance culture.

17 September 2024

Steven Brown
Manager Procurement Operations Pre-qual and Contract Admin
Department of Transport
1 Spring Street
MELBOURNE VIC 3000

Dear Steven,

SPECIALIST TECHNICAL AND ADVISORY SERVICES (TASP) PANEL – INDEXATION OF RATES

I refer to the Specialist and Technical Advisory Services Panel Conditions of Contract between Egis Oceania and
Department of Transport (DoT), dated 13 June 2019. In that contract, Schedule 13 (Indexation of Rates) states
that:
          “(a). Effective from 1 July immediately following the Commencement Date, the Rates will be adjusted
          annually in accordance with the following formula: Adjusted amount = Payment Multiplier X Original
          Amount

           Where: Payment Multiplier – relevant Wage Price Index (Private Sector) published by the Australian
           Bureau of Statistics immediately before the relevant 1 July divided by the Wage Price Index for the
           equivalent quarter in the previous year; and

           Original Amount – the amount (whether previously adjusted or not) applicable immediately prior to the
           relevant 1 July (disregarding rounding (if any) applied to that at the previous 1 July). Provided that, where
           the Payment Multiplier results in a figure less than 1.0, the Payment Multiplier will be 1.0.”



The relevant Wage Price Index change for this period is 4.1%. Accordingly, please refer table below outlining
the rates for this period.

Level 18, 530 Collins Street, Melbourne Victoria 3000 Australia | +61 3 9650 4644 | https://egis-oceania.com.au

Patrick Hunt

                                                (e)   the BOS Contractor has conducted E2E testing in accordance with the Delivery Services SWTR and the E2E testing Test
                                                      Plan;

                                                (f)   the BOS Contractor has issued to the Principal the Monthly Progress Reports from the Contract Date to the scheduled
                                                      Milestone Due Date for this Delivery Milestone;

                                                (g)   the BOS Contractor has, to the Principal's reasonable satisfaction, met all exit criteria for the E2E testing specified in the
                                                      Delivery Services SWTR and the E2E testing Test Plan in accordance with the Delivery Services SWTR; and

                                                (h)   the Final Test Report for E2E testing has been provided to the Principal and has completed the Review Procedures.

                                                      Services SWTR;

                                                      SWTR and the System Acceptance Test Plan;

                                                (e)   the BOS Contractor has provided assistance to the RSS Contractor in conducting the SysAT in accordance with the
                                                      Delivery Services SWTR, the RSS Contractor Interface Deed and as otherwise reasonably required by the Principal;

                                                      Milestone Due Date for this Delivery Milestone in accordance with this Deed; and

                                                      (i)    completed the Delivery Services (other than the Hyper Care Services);

Back Office System Implementation and Support                                                                                    Schedule 17 - Milestone Plan


 No.    Delivery Milestone                      Milestone Achievement Criteria

                                                      (ii)    completed all the relevant Acceptance Tests for the System in accordance with the relevant Test and Acceptance
                                                              Management Plan and the Principal has issued a Notice of Acceptance for each such Acceptance Test;

        Live)

                                                      [8.3] and the Hyper Care Plan;

                                                (d)   the BOS Contractor has satisfied all the entry criteria for the "Test Readiness Review" for "Operational Acceptance
                                                      Testing" as set out in the Delivery Services SWTR and the relevant "Test Plan";

                                                (e)   "Operational Acceptance Testing" has been completed in accordance with the Delivery Services SWTR;

                                                (f)   the "OAT Defect Resolution Period" has been completed, being the period commencing on the Date of Go Live and
                                                      ending on the latest of the following dates:

 No.    Delivery Milestone                      Milestone Achievement Criteria

                                                                      Review Procedures (OAT Minor Defects Plan) for all Minor Defects occurring during the Initial Period
                                                                      and which are not Resolved during the Initial Period;

                                                      out by the BOS Contractor following the issue of the Certificate of Provisional Acceptance have completed the Review
                                                      Procedures; and

                                                (h)   the satisfaction of all other obligations under this Deed that are a condition precedent to achieving Final Acceptance
                                                      occurs to the reasonable satisfaction of the Principal.

                                                                                                                                                              Page 3
            1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

            1.1. Situation
            The North East Link (NEL) State Tolling Corporation (STC) was established under the NEL Act
            (2020). STC must establish a Toll Collection Capability (TCC) that effectively and efficiently collects
            NEL toll revenue – optimising community value to the State and ensuring a scalable State capability
            for future motorways, returning concessions and related opportunities.

            1.2. Challenge
            STC must successfully establish a TCC, concurrent with the delivery of the NEL. STC must consider:
                 •    the timeframe for delivery of the solution, to commence tolling as the NEL road is completed
                      and open
                 •    relevant tolling legislation and regulatory requirements
                 •    interoperability requirements under the MoU and for potential 3rd party retailers (for casual
                      products)
                 •    customer expectations
                 •    service and technology providers in the Global Tolling market and presence in the Australian
                      Tolling market
                 •    potential changes in tolling technology and operational practices
                 •    the opportunity to innovate toll collection practices.

            1.3. The TCC Concept of Operations (ConOps)
            This version of the ConOps reflects on-going evolution from interactions and feedback with
            contractors and operators through the formal engagements undertaken to this point.
            The Concept of Operations will continue to be updated through procurement, delivery and operations.




OFFICIAL SENSITIVE
North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations

                                                                                                        Page 8
            2. TCC CONOPS CONTEXT

            2.1. STC vision
            STC’s vision is:

               A commercially orientated Government owned toll road owner and manager that supports
               DTP’s wider network vision of simple, connected, accessible, reliable and safe journeys.
                STC’s vision describes an aspiration future-state for the Victorian transport system that
               aligns with the direction of the DTP and TIA. It focuses on developing key elements of the
             system – such as simplicity, connection, etc. – for which STC has greater control and license
               to influence in its role as a toll road owner-operator and a key stakeholder to the State in
                                                       transport policy.


            2.2. STC purpose
            STC’s purpose is:

             Protect and enhance the value and legacy of the North East Link Project while exploring ways
                        to unlock shared value with the State using our specialist capabilities
              STC's purpose describes what we exist to do. By contributing to the value and legacy of the
              North East Link Project, we support DTP’s purpose of creating simple, safe, and connected
                                                      journeys.


            2.3. STC values
            STC acknowledge and abide by the Victorian Public Sector core values, from the Public Administration Act 2004
            (PAA). STC has adopted four key values, illustrated in Figure 1.




            Figure 1: STC Values


            2.4. TCC Project Objectives & Guiding Principles

            Objectives of the TCC Project
            The agreed objectives of the toll collection services for the TCC Project are to deliver:
                 •    Flexibility: Maintain flexibility in the operational structure of STC’s toll collection capability to
                      allow for changes that may occur between now and the required operational date
                 •    Entity Agnostic: Ensure the structure can be operated by different entities (including the
                      State, an existing service provider or another external party)




OFFICIAL SENSITIVE
North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations
                                                                                                                              Page 9
                 •    Max Net Revenue: Maximise the collection of tolling revenue, while minimising whole-of-life
                      operational and capital expenditure
                 •    Program: On time, under-budget, and seamless delivery of the full end to end tolling solution,
                      including the Tolling Enabling Infrastructure (TEI), provided by Project Co
                 •    NEL Road User Experience: Ensure the payment of tolls and interaction with STC is simple
                      and convenient, recognising the current toll payment mechanisms available in the market
                 •    Social Licence: Earn, grow, and protect STC’s social licence to operate.
            Guiding Principles of the TCC Project
                 •    Protect Future Options: The selection of a specific option shall not preclude other feasible
                      alternate options being implemented in the future. For example, flexibility to expand to include
                      retail options or other tolling scenarios in line with the needs of the State.
                 •    Minimise Delivery & Operational Risk: Minimise delivery and operational risk with proven
                      robust technology and business practices and positive relationships. The TCC solution is not
                      expected to include new or unproven technologies or solutions
                 •    Future Proof: Ensure that the TCC provides flexibility for future State applications, and to
                      accommodate advances in technology
                 •    Preserve Future Applications for STC: Maximise the opportunity for scalability across other
                      tolling arrangements the State may wish to establish in the future and provide the opportunity
                      for the State to use STC’s capabilities to drive innovation and change in the toll-road sector.

            2.5. Project Overview
            Overall program based on 3 year planning and procurement phase (2022-2026) and 3 year delivery
            phase (2025-2028). The project will be delivered following Victorian government’s, Department of
            Treasury and Finance (DTF), High Value High Risk (HVHR) governance processes.

            Key Assumptions:
                 •    STC procures, delivers and operates the Toll Collection Capability
                 •    STC will not be a Tag issuer or major toll account retailer and will leverage the market already
                      dominated by Interoperability Retailers
                 •    STC will ensure that a suitable solution is available for casual NEL Road Users (with casual
                      use products being available before and after travel, and post-paid trip invoicing for No
                      Arrangement Travel which will be aligned with Victorian Government legislative requirements)
                 •    STC will retain flexibility to accommodate an evolving market for retail, technology, customer
                      expectations, and payment options. The procured TCC BOS solution may have existing
                      defined products and customer operations functionality, such as retail tag and video account
                      management, as built in the solution that could be activated for STC at a later date.
                 •    The TCC selection criteria will include consideration of the TCC solutions ability to
                      accommodate emerging tolling technologies, commercial arrangements, future toll roads and
                      revenue opportunities – but not at the expense of NEL delivery outcomes and timeframes.
                      STC must have a reliable revenue collection system ready for the opening of the toll road
                 •    Road User Charging (RUC) is explicitly excluded from the TCC scope.
                 •    STC project governance and DTF HVHR framework applies to the TCC procurement process
                 •    Project Co (Spark) will design, build and maintain the Tolling Enabling Infrastructure (TEI).
                      The successful TCC Roadside Systems (RSS) contractor will be required to provide a
                      solution that interfaces with the TEI. The TEI requirements have been specified based on a
                      single gantry structure spanning the entire width of the carriageway with sufficient access for
                      maintenance (without impeding traffic flow), and connections to tolling cabinets for power and




OFFICIAL SENSITIVE
North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations
                                                                                                                         Page 10
                      network communications (full details are provided in the extract of Part H21 of the PSDR).
                      The TCC contractor will also be required to accede to the Tolling Interface Deed alongside
                      STC and Project Co under a tripartite arrangement. The Tolling Interface Deed defines the
                      necessary and important interface controls between the successful TCC and the TEI
                 •    The TCC RSS contractor will be required to design, manufacture, install and maintain the
                      gantry structure that will be installed on the footings provided in the TEI.
                 •    TCC delivery is planned to be ready prior to the completion of the road to reduce the delivery
                      risk and enable a readiness program for STC operations and the solution must be capable of
                      being deployed as soon as possible once the NEL is ready for the RSS to be deployed
                      successfully.
                 •    The TCC must allow for STC to operate it internally or outsource independent functions as
                      required (e.g. image processing, call centre, debt collection, etc.).
            Program & Approach
            The TCC is currently planned to be procured and delivered generally in line with the following
            program, subject to final government approvals:
              Program                                                       Date
              Market Sounding                                               2022 – 2023 (Q4 2022 to Q1 2023) - Completed
              EOI RSS release                                               Q4 2023 - Completed
              EOI RSS Shortlist announced                                   Q2 2024 - Completed
              EOI BOS release                                               Q4 2024
              EOI BOS Shortlist announced                                   Q1 2025
              RFP RSS release                                               Q3 2024 - Completed
              RFP BOS release                                               Q2 2025
              RSS Contract Award                                            Q2 2025
              BOS Contract Award                                            Q2 2026
              TCC Operational Readiness                                     mid 2028

            Table 2: TCC Program

            Operating models, technology solution, contractual framework for delivery and operating phases will
            be further refined after the EOI phase prior to being defined in the RFT.

                                                                                                                                Page 15
            4.2. Scenario 1: Existing Interoperable Toll Account Customer

            Primary scenario
                      1. Road User Travel
            Mark Thompson is transporting goods in his truck from Sydney to a business in Melbourne’s south
            eastern suburbs. Mark has an E-Toll account and his vehicle is fitted with an E-Toll tag. Mark’s E-Toll
            account is active and setup with automatic payments. Mark travels on NEL and when passing through
            a NEL toll point Mark hears a single beep from his E-Toll tag. Mark continues on his journey to his
            destination knowing that his trip on NEL will be charged to his E-Toll account.
            Later when Mark views his E-Toll account he can see the charge for his trip on NEL.
                      2. Passage Detected
            As Mark’s truck enters the tollway, the STC TCC detects and identifies his entry using the tag
            provided by E-Toll.
            The STC TCC records the details of Mark’s passage (his tag and vehicle) with sufficient detail to be
            able to satisfy the legal evidence requirements while ensuring that only a single passage and trip
            record is recorded (no duplicates).
                      3. Trip Constructed, Classified and Rated
            The STC TCC completes a calculation of the trip completed by the vehicle, confirms the vehicle
            classification via its LPN (using a lookup process) and with reference to STC TCC’s records of the
            vehicle (tag) calculates the toll applicable to his journey.
                      4. Trip Routed
            Based upon the detection of the unique identifier (eTag identifier), STC TCC is able to consult an
            interoperability register and identify the applicable retailer account to be charged for the trip. STC
            submits a payment claim that includes the relevant details including the Toll and Fees applicable to
            Mark’s trip.
                      5. Account charged and Settled with STC
            The interoperability retailer confirms that Mark’s account is in order and accepts the charges on behalf
            of its customer. As Mark’s retailer is interoperable the daily Australian MoU batch process is utilised
            and Mark’s account is updated some time later with the charges as determined by the retailer.
            The retailer remits the Toll and Fees owing for Mark’s trip, less any fee due to the Retailer (Discount
            Amount) with STC reconciling this leveraging the MOU framework that both parties have signed up to.
                      6. Customer Enquiry
            When Mark gets his next statement from his tolling retailer, he notes that there is a problem with the
            toll charged. He calls / emails / contacts his retailer to resolve the issue – the Retailer action taken is
            independent of any outstanding issues with STC
            Scenario Specific Assumptions
                 •    Customer has a pre-existing current toll tag account with an Interoperable Retailer.
                 •    The TCC Interoperable Retailer Register has a commencement and expiry date, allowing for
                      ‘back dating of effective date.
                 •    The Foreign Toll Operator ‘Hub’ or gateway will continue to be used to manage Interoperable
                      Retailer arrangements (Black and white lists’).




OFFICIAL SENSITIVE
North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations
                                                                                                                          Page 16
            Figure 3. Existing Interoperable Toll Account Customer

            4.3. Scenario 2: Road User account updated after travel

            Primary scenario
                      1. NEL Road User Travels
            David Anderson is travelling from Balwyn to Macleod. David has a Linkt account however his vehicle
            is being repaired and he is using a loan vehicle.
                      2. Passage Detected
            As David’s car enters the tollway, the STC TCC detects and identifies his vehicle.
            The STC TCC records and stores the details of David’s trip (that of his vehicle) with sufficient detail to
            be able to satisfy the legal evidence requirements and establish the vehicle class.
                      3. Trip Constructed, Classified and Rated
            The STC TCC determines the vehicle class and completes a calculation of the trip completed by the
            vehicle and calculates the toll applicable to his journey.
                      4. Trip Routed
            The STC TCC looks up the tolling account register(s) and finds that the LPN is not registered with a
            payment method. The STC TCC flags/stores the trip for review periodically and for several days after
            the travel date as configured in the TCC system.
            When David arrives at work (after travelling on NEL), he adds his LPN of his vehicle to his account
            and receives verification. His account retailer adds his details to the TCC register of authorised road
            users (assuming back dated travel is allowed).
            When the STC TCC next consults the TCC Arrangement Register, David has added his LPN to his
            preferred retailer, and the STC TCC is able to locate David’s account to be charged for the trip.
                 5&6. Account charged
            STC charges the applicable retailer for the trip (including any applicable administration fees) and
            passes the trip details to the retailer for settlement. David’s preferred retailer updates his account in
            accordance with the Retailer’s standard of service.
            Account charged and Settled with STC as for Scenario 1
                 7. Customer Enquiry
            [As for Scenario 1]
            Scenario Specific Assumptions
                 •    Customer is an existing Interoperability Retailer account holder in good standing.

North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations
                                                                                                                          Page 18
            Figure 4. First Time Traveller, Account Opened after Travel

            4.4. Scenario 3: No Arrangement Travel

            Primary Scenario
                      1. Road User Travels
            Emily Carter is travelling from Nunawading to Campbellfield and uses the NEL. Emily’s vehicle is
            registered in Victoria but is not linked to a tolling account and she has not purchased a Casual Use
            Product. Several days after travelling on NEL Emily receives a Toll Notice for the unpaid travel on
            NEL.




OFFICIAL SENSITIVE
North East Link State Tolling Corporation
Concept of Operations
                                                                                                                                     Page 19
                      2. Passage Detected
            Emily’s car is detected by the TCC on her travel on the NEL.
                      3. Trip Constructed, Classified and Rated
            As for Scenario 1
                      4. Trip Routed
            TCC is unable to locate Emily’s car on the TCC Retailer Register, and the LPN is assigned as No
            Arrangement Travel. A configured number of days later when a search for Emily’s LPN is conducted,
            no valid arrangement can be located.
            The TCC generates toll notices and manages an escalating cycle of notices and fees in an attempt to
            recover the unpaid tolls.
                      5. Issue Toll Notice
            Emily receives her toll notice (In the post or electronically via email or SMS if they have been provided
            from the registry) and she makes payment as shown on the notice.
                      6. Customer queries charge
            In the event that Emily does not pay, and the issue proceeds to debt recovery the TCC is able to
            generate a court file of enforceable evidence that can prove the trip was taken, and that it was Emily’s
            vehicle. At this stage, it is expected that this evidence pack will include a date/time stamped image
            with chain of custody requirements met (alternate electronic evidence may be applicable at the time of
            TCC operation). The ability of the TCC to accurately identify each vehicle LPN and record that trip
            correctly is critical.
            Scenario Specific Assumptions
                 •    No arrangement established
                 •    Once-off travel, no pattern of use
                 •    STC will require the ability to choose to refer to an external Debt Collection Agency or take
                      enforcement action (in line with the legislative provisions).

            Victoria Dispatcher plots the fastest route to the location of the emergency incident which includes
            using the NEL toll road. The route is sent to the Paramedics responding to the incident.

1.   Glossary

Term                    Meaning

                        Means, as part of the Tolling Collection Capability, the system that receives data recording
                        the passage of vehicles from the RSS. The BOS: identifies and rates trips by vehicles,
Back Office System or   creates, and processes payment request files that can be provided to other tolling operators
BOS                     to collect toll payments in respect of those trips made by their customers. Manages the
                        purchase and use of casual user products, and allows for debt recovery by STC or
                        enforcement by relevant government agencies in respect of no arrangement travel.

BOS Contract            Means the document entitled ‘Back Office System Implementation and Support
                        Agreement’ between the STC and BOS Contractor

BOS Contractor          Means the person that has entered into an agreement with STC substantially in the form of
                        the BOS Contract.

NEL STC – Independent Verifer Services RFP                                                        Page 4 of 17
                                                     OFFICIAL
3.   BACKGROUND
     As a priority transport infrastructure investment by the State of Victoria (the State), North East Link (NEL)
     will provide a safe and efficient freeway connection by improving traffic flow, reducing travel times,
     removing non local traffic from local roads and increasing road use reliability for up to 135,000 vehicles a
     day. NEL will take 15,000 trucks off busy residential roads in the north east of greater Melbourne each
     day and reduce traffic on the arterial road network crossing the Yarra River. NEL will enhance access to
     major suburban business and employment centres, improve orbital road connectivity acro ss Melbourne
     and boost the capacity of the city’s freight network.
     North East Link will include the North East Link tollway (NEL Tollway), with the North East Link State Tolling
     Corporation (STC) retaining the entitlement to collect toll revenue.
     STC is a public entity body corporate established under the North East Link Act 2020 (Vic) (NEL Act). Its
     purpose is to:
         •    operate, maintain and otherwise manage the North East Link road, including managing and
              controlling the use of and access to the North East Link road;
         •    procure, deliver and operate the NEL tolling system;
         •    fix and collect tolls for use of the NEL Tollway; and
         •    optimise the value of, or return from, STC’s infrastructure and other assets.
     In October 2021, STC and the State executed the NEL Tolling Agreement which sets out the terms on which
     STC may fix and collect tolls and fees for the use of the NEL Tollway (or part of it) for the passage of
     vehicles. STC is continuing to establish its Toll Collection Capability (TCC) for the NEL Tollway, which forms
     part of the North East Link Program.
     STC has proposed to develop an end to end solution for the TCC that incorporates:
         •    the delivery and operation of a roadside system (RSS);
         •    the delivery, support, and maintenance of a back office system (BOS); and
         •    outcomes of the TCC Information Technology (TCC IT) Project, including the provision of
              supporting communications networks, IT infrastructure and related services.
     STC is procuring these elements of the TCC through separate, staggered approaches to market. To support
     STC in the delivery of these packages, STC will engage an independent verifier.


4.   PURPOSE
     The purpose of the TCC Independent Verifier (IV) Services is to provide STC with an independent expert
     opinion that the specified technical and business requirements have been met as per the TCC Contracts.
     The TCC Contracts include the Scope of Works and Technical Requirements.
     The TCC IV Services will include design and document reviews, witnessing of tests and demonstrations to
     ensure that the requirements verification traceability matrix is complete, accurate, and records sufficient
     evidence to verify that the requirements within the TCC Contracts have been met.
     The role will not have a commercial or financial element i.e. there is no payment certification role and
     there is no need to issue formal certificates to verify payment milestones.




NEL STC – Independent Verifer Services RFP                                                            Page 5 of 17
                                                         OFFICIAL
5.   REQUIREMENTS AND DELIVERABLES
     The TCC IV will be expected to use its expert technical, assurance and contractual expertise to assist
     STC in monitoring and reporting on the level of compliance that the TCC Contractors (the RSS and BOS
     contractors) demonstrate in accordance with the TCC Contracts and the documented management plans.

     The TCC IV will provide expert advice and report on a monthly basis to the tolling director and will be
     expected to brief other nominated stakeholders on the review services as may be required.

     The TCC IV Services (the Services) are to be provided through the delivery stages of the TCC Project –
     including the implementation and operational readiness phases due to complete by December 2028 and
     then up to the first 3 months of operations (subject to the extent of defects identified during the initial
     operations period).
     The TCC IV will be responsible for delivering the following Services:

     (a) Development and submission of an Independent Verifier Plan (within 20 business days of
         commencement) detailing the methodology, process and approach of performing the Services
         including the skills, expertise and experience required of the resources and the estimated resource
         levels required for each component of the Services. This Independent Verifier Plan is to be agreed
         with STC.
     (b) Familiarisation with documentation that forms the relevant TCC Contracts (including TCC Contractor
         management plans) and the North East Link Act 2020.
     (c) Attendance at meetings with both STC and the TCC Contractors where clarifications and
         understanding of the requirements will be further explored.
     (d) Reviewing and evaluating (by general overview and reasonable checking (GORC)) or as directed by
         the tolling director, the TCC Contractor’s performance against the obligations imposed in the relevant
         TCC Contract.
     (e) Expressing an informed opinion on the TTC Contract deliverables including the achievement of formal
         entry and exit criteria detailed in the TCC Contracts for each deliverable or project milestone/phase,
         and whether that deliverable is suitable for endorsement or acceptance under the terms of the TCC
         Contracts.
     (f) Reviewing evidence submitted by the TCC Contractor in order to provide an opinion on whether the
         system complies with the TCC project SWTRs for RSS and BOS including witnessing of tests and
         demonstrations provided as evidence to support the achievement of the requirements contained in
         the TCC Contracts.
     (g) Recommend a program of TCC Contractor verification audits relevant to the performance of the TCC
         Contractor’s obligations under the TCC Contracts and where requested by STC conduct or assist
         STC in the conduct of the audits and report to STC on its findings and any recommendations arising
         from the audit.
     (h) Providing progress reports to the Project Control Group (PCG) in accordance with an agreed
         timetable monthly based on:
              i. A statement of the IV activities performed during the period;
              ii. A forecast of the IV activities to be conducted within the next period;
              iii. regular observation of the status of the TCC Contractor’s progress against the schedule;
              iv. witnessing formal test sessions and internal audits;
              v. reviewing progress reports;
              vi. conducting meetings with key personnel within the TCC Project Team; and
              vii. Identifying any major risks or concerns that need to be raised to the PCG in relation to the IV
                   observations.
     (i) The option for STC to elect an independent review be conducted by the Independent Verifier, of the
         readiness of the systems, processes and people required to enable STC to commence the tolling
         operations for North East Link. This review will include:
              i. Ensuring the contract documents are in place and up to date;
              ii. System testing is completed successfully and there are no impediments to operations
                   commencing;
              iii. Users are ready to operate the systems and the business is ready to implement the changes;
              iv. STC supporting systems are in place and ready to go; and
              v. Support and maintenance arrangements are in place and have been validated.




NEL STC – Independent Verifer Services RFP                                                           Page 6 of 17
                                                       OFFICIAL
    (j) The option for STC to elect, following the date of Operations Phase Commencement (Go Live), (as
        set out in section 6) a review of the initial operations to identify any observations or issues that
        should be brought to the attention of the tolling director and TCC tolling operations manager.
    (k) Perform any other tasks that should reasonably be anticipated by an experienced and competent
        professional provider of IV Services being necessary for the intended objectives of the TCC IV
        Services.

    The TCC IV should not engage directly with any of the TCC Contractors in any form of communication,
    negotiation, or coordination regarding project-related matters without authorisation from STC.
    Exclusions from the Scope:
    The following items are explicitly excluded from the Services:

          •   Contract administration services;
          •   Payment certification services;
          •   Defect certification services;
          •   Review of the civil and structure elements of the tolling point structures;
          •   Independent verification services for the TCC IT Project; and
          •   Verification of the TCC Contractor’s processes, procedures and policies that are not deliverables
              under the TCC Contracts.

                                                       OFFICIAL
10. Fair Jobs Code:
    Overview
    The Fair Jobs Code (FJC) aims to improve employment outcomes for persons employed by suppliers and
    service providers to the Victorian Government. It is implemented by Victorian Government departments,
    agencies and public bodies, such as STC, to support and promote fair labour standards and ensure
    compliance with employment law. It applies to the purchase of goods and/or services regardless of the
    method of procurement.

    A recent policy update means that from 1 September 2024 the FJC applies to threshold procurement
    contracts with a value of $1 million or more exclusive of GST. Should the Supplier’s total fee exceed this
    threshold value, the Supplier must complete Section 3, Item 5 to demonstrate compliance to the FJC.


    To comply with the FJC, the Supplier must:

         1.    hold a valid Fair Jobs Code Pre-Assessment Certificate, available at buyingfor.vic.gov.au/fair-
               jobs-code-departments-and-agencies. A copy of the Supplier’s Pre-Assessment Certificate
               number must be included in a response to this RFP.
               Suppliers that do not hold a valid Pre-Assessment Certificate may not be considered for this
               procurement. If a Supplier is unable to secure a valid Pre-Assessment Certificate, it must
               notify STC as soon as possible and prior to submitting its bid.
               STC may use its discretion to enter into a contract with a Supplier that does not have a valid
               Pre-Assessment Certificate subject to sections 4.3 or 4.4 of the FJC.
         2.    if successful, maintain a valid Pre-Assessment Certificate throughout any agreement entered
               into between the Supplier and STC. That agreement will also include the FJC Model Clauses.
         3.    if the Supplier’s Pre-Assessment Certificate is revoked or lapses after a response is submitted,
               but before contracts are awarded, notify STC as soon as practicable but not later than ten (10)
               days after the revocation or expiry date.
    Further information and assistance

    The FJC Guidelines provide guidance on the application of the FJC and are available at
    buyingfor.vic.gov.au/fair-jobs-code-departments-and-agencies.

    The FJC Unit provides information to assist Suppliers with Pre-Assessment Certificates. For further
    information or assistance, Suppliers can contact the FJC Unit:
    Ph: 13 22 15    Email: fairjobscode@ecodev.vic.gov.au
